    terminal re-deriving the entitlement list and the expiry by hand for every sale.
  - **The gap I found (confirmed in code, not invented).** `vh trust license issue` (`trustledger/cli.js:1746`)
    REQUIRES the human to pass `--entitlements <comma-list>` AND a hand-computed `--expires <ISO>` for EVERY sale.
    There is NO plan catalog anywhere (grep for plan-catalog/fulfill/webhook over `trustledger/ cli/ docs/ test/`
    returns nothing): the mapping from "what the customer bought" (a `planId`) to `{entitlements, term}` lives only
    in the seller's head. That makes fulfillment (a) error-prone — a typo in the flag grants the wrong tier, a
    hand-computed expiry drifts — and (b) UN-AUTOMATABLE: a Stripe/Paddle "payment succeeded" event carries a PLAN
    id and a PAID-THROUGH date, never a comma-list of `multi_state_policy,seal,...` flags. So P-6 step (3) ("issue a
    license to each paying customer … renew on each billing period") is a manual terminal step per sale — the exact
    thing that makes self-serve revenue impossible. The CLOSED `ENTITLEMENTS` table already exists
    (`trustledger/license.js:61`); the missing piece is the machine-readable plan→entitlements catalog over it and a
    pure order→license mapping the gate already trusts the output of.
  - **The move (EPIC-37, three tasks).** T-37.1: `trustledger/plans.js` — a versioned, STRICTLY-validated plan
    CATALOG (`validatePlanCatalog`, pure, I/O-free) mapping each `planId → {displayName, entitlements[], term}` over
    the CLOSED `ENTITLEMENTS` set, with bundled `trustledger/fixtures/plans/*.json` DRAFT skeletons (price/term are
    the seller's data, NOT decided by the loop); an unknown entitlement, a duplicate planId, a non-positive term, or
    a wrong kind/schema is a HARD reject (never a silent mis-grant), mirroring `policy.js`'s posture. T-37.2: a pure
    `fulfillOrder({plan, customer, paidThrough|term, issuedAt}, catalog)` that resolves the plan, derives
    `expiresAt` (from `paidThrough`, or `issuedAt + term`), and returns the EXACT `buildLicensePayload` params —
    deterministic (same order + catalog ⇒ byte-identical fields) — plus `vh trust license fulfill --plan <id>
    --customer <name> (--paid-through <ISO> | uses the plan term) --key-env/--key-file <…> [--out]` that reads the
    human-supplied key (read-used-discarded, the EXACT posture of `license issue` / `vh dataset sign`; the loop NEVER
    holds a key), looks up the plan, and emits the SAME signed `*.vhlicense.json` the existing `verify`/CLI-gate/web
    gate already ACCEPT (proved by round-tripping a `fulfill`ed license through `vh trust license verify` and a
    gated `reconcile --license`). T-37.3: document "Plan catalog & fulfillment" in `docs/TRUSTLEDGER.md`, show the
    one-command webhook-handler shape, restate the boundary VERBATIM (the loop ships the catalog + mapping; the price,
    the vendor key, and the actual webhook/billing are human steps), and SHARPEN P-6 step (3) accordingly.
  - **Why higher-leverage than the alternatives.** (a) A 7th P-8 de-risk is the marginal vein the directive
    explicitly warns against, and the SALES-call blocker is a human action no build can move. (b) Re-sharpening
    P-3/P-5/P-7 is forbidden busywork — they are decision-ready. (c) A new product surface is the capped vein nine
    mechanism epics already proved doesn't move usefulness. (d) A hosted billing/Stripe integration is an
    outward/funds human step (stays P-6) — but the loop-buildable half (the deterministic order→license mapping the
    webhook calls) is EXACTLY what makes that human step "point your existing webhook at one command + fill in the
    price column" instead of "design a fulfillment system from scratch." This adds a NEW capability — self-serve
    fulfillment — that unlocks a revenue motion the loop has never built toward, and it directly unblocks P-6 once
    the human provisions a key + sets prices.
  - **Guardrails respected. REVENUE INTEGRITY upheld.** Pure-local, OFFLINE, deterministic; the catalog + mapping
    are PURE/I-O-free, `fulfill` reads the human's key read-used-discarded (ephemeral `Wallet.createRandom()` in
    tests ONLY — the loop NEVER generates, persists, logs, or holds a real key), opens no socket, takes no payment.
    STRICTLY ADDITIVE + NON-REGRESSING: the existing `license issue`/`verify`, the CLI + web gate, the closed
    `ENTITLEMENTS` table, and every EPIC-1..36 test stay green; `fulfill` emits a container BYTE-COMPATIBLE with what
    those already accept; the test COMMAND is unchanged. NO token/coin/NFT/sale/yield, NO funds, NO deploy. Income
    remains a paid SUBSCRIPTION/license for delivered software value (the free tier stays open) — an access
    credential, NOT a tradeable/appreciating asset. NO NEW `needs-human` item; this SHARPENS P-6 step (3) and changes
    none of P-3/P-5/P-7/P-8.

    invent more incremental tasks; SHARPEN the blocking needs-human ask and prefer auto-buildable work that

  - **The gap I found (confirmed in code, not invented).** The product is a try-before-you-buy FREE tier
    (`cli/evidence.js:56` `SAMPLE_LIMIT = 25`): an UNSIGNED `vh.evidence-seal` of up to 25 files is FREE; SIGNING
    (`evidence_signed`) and sealing >25 files (`evidence_unlimited`) are the PAID entitlements. EPIC-35 made the
    FREE VERIFY side zero-install (`verifier/dist/verify-vh-standalone.js`). But the FREE PRODUCE side is still
    gated behind cloning the repo and `npm install` of the heavy `ethers`/`hardhat` stack — `vh evidence seal`
    runs through `cli/evidence.js` → `cli/core/packetseal.js` → `cli/hash.js`, and `cli/hash.js:44` pulls
    `keccak256/concat/toUtf8Bytes` from `ethers`. So a prospect handed a seal can verify it in 10 seconds with
    zero install, but CANNOT produce one of their OWN to hand to a counterparty without a clone+install or a sales
    call. The self-service adoption loop is HALF-OPEN. Crucially, the free-tier seal needs NO signing, NO key, NO
    secp256k1 — only the path-bound keccak/merkle convention that is ALREADY VENDORED in
    `verifier/lib/{keccak256-vendored,merkle,canonical}.js`, so a zero-install free sealer reuses the exact tested
    crypto and its output re-derives byte-for-byte through the existing standalone verifier.
  - **The move (EPIC-36, three tasks).** T-36.1: a pure, dependency-free `verifier/lib/seal-evidence.js` that

    core, with NO signing path. T-36.2: generalize the existing deterministic bundler to ALSO emit

    `--sign`/`--license`/`--key` flag exists), and opens NO socket (EPIC-31 poison guard). T-36.3: document the

    restating the honest boundary VERBATIM and naming the paid SIGN/UNLIMITED upgrade so the free loop is the funnel.
  - **Why higher-leverage than the alternatives.** (a) A 6th de-risk of P-8 is the marginal vein the directive

  ARTIFACT EVERY needs-human GATE WAITS ON — an end-to-end, OFFLINE, EPHEMERAL-KEY DESIGN-PARTNER PILOT KIT a human can

  No stack change (plain Node JS under a new `pilot/` tree, reusing the existing `cli/`/`trustledger/`/`verifier/`
  entrypoints; tests under the unchanged `npx hardhat test`).
  - **Stagnation + persistent value-ceiling read (acted on, not recited).** PERSISTENT VALUE CEILING with a REGRESSION the

    pinned at 3, humanGated STANDING at 3-5 across 6+ runs. Build frontier EMPTY — EPIC-22..31 ALL VERIFIED, 1660 tests
    green; only `needs-decision`/`needs-human` TODOs remain (EPIC-3/4). Crucially, the PREVIOUS run already executed the
    "material pivot" (EPIC-31 independent verifier) and usefulness STILL dropped — proving the bottleneck is no longer a
    missing mechanism. The directive for a STANDING humanGated count is explicit: do NOT invent more incremental tasks;
    SHARPEN the blocking needs-human ask and prefer auto-buildable work that DE-RISKS / directly UNBLOCKS it.
  - **The gap I found (confirmed in code, not invented).** EVERY revenue gate — P-3 (DataLedger trust-root pilot), P-5/P-6
    (TrustLedger CPA + delivery), P-7 (evidence vendor key + B2B design partner) — waits on the SAME human action: "land a
    design partner / run a pilot." The loop has built every mechanism that pilot needs (reconcile, policy, close, inspect,
    seal, license issue/verify, evidence seal/verify, EPIC-31 independent `verify-vh`) — but they are SCATTERED across CLIs
    and docs. The one existing runnable demo (`examples/run.js`) covers ONLY DataLedger + ProofParcel — it never touches
    TrustLedger reconcile, the license gate, the evidence packet, OR the counterparty `verify-vh` hand-off, which are
    exactly the surfaces P-5/P-6/P-7 are sold on. So a human starting a pilot today must hand-assemble the journey from a
    dozen man pages. THAT assembly — not another mechanism — is the missing, fully-auto-buildable thing.
  - **The move (assemble, don't add).** T-32.1 builds `pilot/run-pilot.js`: a self-contained, OFFLINE, ephemeral-key kit
    that drives the REAL evidence journey — issue a license with a `Wallet.createRandom()` vendor key, `evidence seal --sign`
    GATED by it (and ASSERT the paid `--sign` is refused without a valid license), HAND OFF only the packet to the
    INDEPENDENT `verify-vh` (assert OK), then TAMPER and assert REJECT — printing one PASS/FAIL verdict, writing only to a
    temp workspace, ending at the explicit human handoff. T-32.2 extends it to ALSO drive the TrustLedger RECONCILE vertical
    end to end (license-gated paid surface + reconciliation seal independently verified + tamper rejected), folded into the
    SAME single verdict. T-32.3 ships the buyer-facing `docs/PILOT.md` + `pilot/README.md` runbook and a CONSOLIDATED P-8
    that folds the shared "land a design partner" precondition of P-3/P-5/P-6/P-7 into ONE decision-ready ask whose
    deliverable IS this kit.
  - **Why higher-leverage than another increment.** It does not add surface — it makes the surface SELLABLE by handing the
    human the exact artifact every gate waits on, de-risking ALL of P-3/P-5/P-6/P-7 at once through NO new human gate. Nine
    mechanism epics and an independent-verifier pivot could not move usefulness because the missing thing was never more
    mechanism; it was the CONSOLIDATED, runnable, hand-it-to-a-partner proof that the mechanisms work together.
  - **Why it beats the alternatives I considered.** (a) A tenth mechanism is the capped vein the regression warns against.
    (b) Re-sharpening P-3/P-5/P-6/P-7 individually is forbidden busywork — each is already sharp in isolation; the missing
    thing is the CONSOLIDATED handoff (P-8). (c) Extending `examples/run.js` in place would entangle the buyer journey with
    the existing DataLedger demo and break its tight test; a clean `pilot/` tree keeps both. (d) A hosted/interactive demo
    is an outward/network human step and re-introduces "trust the vendor's server."
  - **Guardrails respected. REVENUE INTEGRITY upheld.** Pure-local, OFFLINE, deterministic, READ-ONLY of the human's key
    (ephemeral `Wallet.createRandom()` test keys ONLY — the kit NEVER creates/holds/persists a real key); NO token/coin/NFT/
    sale/yield, NO funds, NO deploy. STRICTLY ADDITIVE + NON-REGRESSING: a new `pilot/` tree changes no producer code, every
    EPIC-1..31 test stays green, and the test COMMAND is unchanged. Income = a license/subscription for delivered software
    value the kit demonstrates — the license is an access credential, NOT a tradeable/appreciating asset.
  - **T-32.3 done (Builder note, NO new human gate).** Shipped the buyer-facing runbook `docs/PILOT.md` (a NON-AUTHOR can

- **2026-06-24 — Strategist: STOP ADDING PRODUCT SURFACE AND BUILD THE ONE CROSS-VERTICAL CAPABILITY THAT MAKES THE
  FAMILY'S CORE PROMISE REAL — an INDEPENDENT, near-zero-dependency, offline VERIFIER a COUNTERPARTY can run to confirm
  any verifyhash artifact WITHOUT installing the producer's stack. Open EPIC-31. This is a MATERIAL change of approach,
  not a tenth product-surface increment.** No stack change (the verifier lives in its OWN `verifier/` tree, plain Node +
  `js-sha3`, explicitly NO ethers/hardhat; specs run under the unchanged `npx hardhat test`).
  - **Stagnation + value-ceiling read (acted on, not recited).** Textbook QUALITY STAGNATION + a GROWING value ceiling:
    avgUsefulness REGRESSED then went flat (4.0 → 3.75 → 3.75 → 3.5 → 3.75 → 3.75), minUsefulness stuck at 3, and
    humanGated CLIMBED 3 → 3 → 3 → 3 → 3 → 5. Build frontier EMPTY (EPIC-22..30 all VERIFIED, 1625 tests green).
    EPIC-22..30 are NINE+ consecutive product-surface increments (TrustLedger engine/policy/close/ingest/seal/web/
    onboarding/entitlement, then the EPIC-30 evidence harvest). EVERY revenue path is dammed behind a HUMAN go-to-market
    step that no building can move — P-5/P-6 (TrustLedger legal/CPA/pricing) and now P-7 (evidence vendor key + design
    partner). The directive for this state is explicit: change approach MATERIALLY toward a capability that unlocks NEW
    value AND de-risks the dam — NOT another increment. All of P-5/P-6/P-7 are already decision-ready; re-touching them
    is forbidden busywork. So this is a genuinely DIFFERENT KIND of work.
  - **The gap I found (confirmed in code, not invented).** The SINGLE load-bearing selling proposition of the WHOLE
    family — TrustLedger seals, evidence packets, dataset attestations, proof bundles, RFC-3161 timestamps — is "you do
    NOT have to trust the producer; verify it OFFLINE, independently." I traced the verify path: every signed artifact's
    verification routes through `cli/core/attestation.js`, which `require("ethers")` (line 27: `verifyMessage`,
    `getAddress`, `Wallet`), and the package's only install surface pulls `ethers` + `hardhat` +
    `@nomicfoundation/hardhat-toolbox`. So the party who matters MOST for a sale — the COUNTERPARTY (auditor, opposing
    counsel, the buyer's security team, the design partner deciding whether to pay) — can only "independently" verify by
    `npm install`-ing the FULL, heavy, unauditable-in-an-afternoon stack OF THE VERY VENDOR whose claim they are trying
    to check independently. That is a direct CONTRADICTION of the core promise and a concrete adoption + WTP blocker on
    EVERY vertical at once. The signing scheme is, however, simple and documented: keccak256 (`js-sha3`, already a
    runtime dep) + EIP-191 `eip191-personal-sign` (a 65-byte r||s||v secp256k1 sig over canonical UTF-8 bytes) — fully
    reproducible WITHOUT ethers.
  - **The move (build the missing independent verifier; multiply every vertical from one small surface).** T-31.1 stands
    up a `verifier/` core that re-derives keccak roots + recovers the EIP-191 secp256k1 signer using ONLY `js-sha3` +
    Node `crypto` (or a tiny vendored secp256k1 routine), with a CROSS-CHECK test proving it returns the byte-identical
    address to the production `cli/core/attestation.js`/ethers path (the anti-divergence guard). T-31.2 ships
    `verify-vh <artifact>` — a standalone, read-only, offline command that auto-detects the artifact kind, re-derives the
    root, recovers + pins the signer, and prints OK / which file CHANGED/MISSING / `bad_signature` / `wrong_issuer` with
    CI exit codes — installable ALONE via its own `verifier/package.json` (NO ethers/hardhat). T-31.3 documents it as a
    self-explaining buyer deliverable and adds an ISOLATION test that mechanically PROVES the verifier pulls in no
    producer code and opens no network handle.
  - **Why this is genuinely higher-leverage than another increment.** It makes the family's HEADLINE claim actually true
    for the buyer, multiplies value across ALL verticals from one small surface, and directly DE-RISKS P-7 + P-3/P-4
    (counterparty confidence IS the WTP) — through NO new human gate. Nine product-surface increments could not move the
    needle because the missing thing was never more surface; it was the buyer's ability to TRUST the surface without
    trusting us.
  - **Why this beats the alternatives I considered.** (a) A tenth product-surface increment is the capped vein the
    regression + growing humanGated warn against. (b) Re-sharpening P-5/P-6/P-7 is forbidden busywork; all decision-ready.
    (c) "Tell buyers to install the CLI" is the exact non-starter that contradicts the independence claim. (d) A hosted
    verifier is an outward/network human step and re-introduces "trust the vendor's server."
  - **Guardrails respected. REVENUE INTEGRITY upheld.** Pure-local, OFFLINE, deterministic, READ-ONLY (the verifier NEVER
    signs, holds a key, or writes cwd); NO crypto-token/coin/NFT/sale/yield, NO funds, NO deploy, NO real key (ephemeral
    `Wallet.createRandom()` test keys ONLY). STRICTLY ADDITIVE + NON-REGRESSING: the verifier lives in its own `verifier/`
    tree, changes NO producer code, and its independent crypto is cross-checked against production so it can never
    silently diverge; every EPIC-1..30 test stays green and the test COMMAND is unchanged. This is a trust-multiplier for
    delivered software value, NOT itself a tradeable/appreciating asset.
  - **T-31.3 done (Builder note, no new human gate).** The independent verifier is now a self-contained buyer deliverable:
    a counterparty-facing `verifier/README.md` + `docs/INDEPENDENT-VERIFICATION.md` (exact bytes verified, EIP-191/keccak
    scheme, the FREE/no-network posture, the honest trust boundary, a worked seal→hand-over→`verify-vh` example), the main
    README links both, and `test/verifier.isolation.test.js` MECHANICALLY proves the independence claim (static grep of
    every `require(` in `verifier/` for ethers/hardhat/@nomicfoundation/cli/trustledger back-edges + a real verify run
    under a poisoned network that asserts NO socket is opened). **Cross-reference only (do NOT restate those proposals):**
    this deliverable DE-RISKS **P-3** (the signing/timestamp trust-root — the docs are explicit that `verify-vh` proves
    tamper-evidence + signer-pin, NOT a trusted "sealed at T", which still rides P-3 / the separate RFC-3161 path), **P-4**
    (ProofParcel counterparty confidence), and **P-7** (the evidence design-partner sale) by raising buyer confidence — and
    it introduces **NO new human gate** of its own (pure-local, offline, read-only). P-3/P-4/P-7 stay exactly as written.

    explicit `cfg`, mirroring how `cli/core/manifest.js` already takes a `cfg`), and re-points `trustledger/license.js` at
    it as a THIN adapter — byte-for-byte unchanged TrustLedger behaviour. T-30.2 extracts `cli/core/packetseal.js` (the
    seal core takes the product's `kind` + an OPTIONAL caller header) and re-points `trustledger/seal.js` at it as a thin

    that de-risks the human gate.
  - **The gap I found (confirmed in code, not invented).** The operator pivoted explicitly to usability — "the web
    door is what turns a terminal tool into a product a broker can use" — and EPIC-27 shipped the web front-door. But
    the web surface RE-INTRODUCES the exact pilot-killer EPIC-25 spent a whole epic eliminating on the CLI. I read
    `trustledger/server.js` end to end: it has only two routes (`GET /`, `POST /api/reconcile`); `reconcilePayload`
    calls the STRICT parsers (server.js:146-151) and the first header/cell miss throws an `IngestError` that the UI
    renders as a raw `Error (ingest_error): missing required column "date" ...` (index.html:211-213) — with NO way to
    see what columns the file HAS, what mapped, or how to fix it. The broker who "will never use a terminal" (the
    operator's own framing) CANNOT run `vh trust inspect` and CANNOT pass `--map`. So the single most likely thing to
    kill a P-5 #3 pilot — ingest choking on a real broker's export — is a SELF-SERVICE FIX on the CLI and a DEAD-END
    WALL in the browser. The engine ALREADY has the fix built + tested: `ingest.diagnoseSource(source, text,
    {columnMap})` reports the detected header, the field→column mapping, `requiredMissing`, row/ok counts, a sample,
    and every failing row, and accepts a column-map override. The web door simply doesn't expose it.
  - **The move (the proven CLI capability, repointed at the web surface).** EPIC-25 turned the CLI parse dead-end into
    a self-service fix (`vh trust inspect` + `--map`). EPIC-28 does the IDENTICAL thing for the browser: T-28.1 adds
    `POST /api/inspect` that calls the EXISTING `diagnoseSource` VERBATIM (no re-implemented parsing) + accepts a
    `columnMap` override, with the same named-400/no-cwd-write posture as `/api/reconcile`; T-28.2 makes the page show
    the detected columns and let the broker MAP a missing field from a dropdown of the file's actual headers, then
    thread that map into the real reconcile run; T-28.3 documents it and SHARPENS P-5 #3 so the design-partner
    script's FIRST step ("confirm each file parses") is the BROWSER inspect/map UI for a non-technical broker, not a
    terminal command.
  - **Why this is genuinely higher-leverage than another increment.** The operator's whole thesis is that usability is
    the gating step to a sellable product; a web front-door that drops a cryptic parse error with no recovery is NOT
    usable for the exact buyer it targets. Onboarding (does the broker's real export load, and if not can they
    self-serve a fix WITHOUT a terminal?) is the literal first gate of P-5 #3 and the single technical thing most
    likely to kill the pilot before the engine's correctness is ever seen. Making real files load in the browser — or
    having the page say exactly how to map them — is a NEW capability (self-service web onboarding) on the operator's
    chosen surface, not polish. It connects the two halves of the operator's pivot: EPIC-25's onboarding robustness and
    EPIC-27's web door, which currently don't meet.
  - **Why this beats the alternatives I considered.** (a) Another reconcile/close/policy/seal engine increment is the
    capped vein the regression warns against (six in a row around P-5). (b) Re-sharpening P-5 #1/#2/#3 is busywork —
    they are decision-ready. (c) Exposing the SEAL or close-continuity in the web UI is real future breadth but
    presupposes the file LOADED — onboarding comes first, and a broker can't reach the seal if the parse 400s on file
    one. (d) Multipart/file-upload niceties are cosmetic next to the parse dead-end. (e) Returning to DataLedger/
    ProofParcel is the vein the operator pivoted the lead AWAY from. The web inspect/map is the one auto-buildable
    thing that removes the LEAD product's most likely real-world failure on the operator's chosen surface.
  - **Guardrails respected.** Pure-local, offline, deterministic, NO crypto/token/coin/NFT/sale/yield, NO funds, NO
    deploy, NO real key. No new dependency (reuses the EXISTING `diagnoseSource` + stdlib `http` + vanilla JS; no
    framework, no multipart lib). STRICTLY ADDITIVE: the strict `/api/reconcile` path stays byte-for-byte fail-closed
    (a trust reconciliation must NEVER silently partial-parse); `/api/inspect` is a SEPARATE read-only diagnostic, and
    with no new requests every EPIC-27 test stays green; the test COMMAND is unchanged. REVENUE INTEGRITY unchanged:
    income = a SaaS subscription for a legally-forced monthly chore from paying brokers — the CPA review, the per-state
    policy table, the design partners, hosting (the web door stays a HUMAN deploy step), pricing, and billing all stay
    human steps (P-5). The loop ships only the inspect endpoint + the browser map UI; it must NOT auto-resolve any
    legal meaning, and P-5 stays human-gated.

- **2026-06-24 — OPERATOR DIRECTION: build the TrustLedger WEB UI next (EPIC-27), the highest-value step.**
  Signal: usefulness has slid (4.5→4→3.75→3.5) with rising rework and ~2.2h runs — the CLI reconciliation
  engine is complete + robust, but the loop keeps grinding lower-value BACKEND polish (seals, ingest aliases)
  and has NOT pivoted to usability on its own. A property-management broker will never use a terminal, so the
  product is currently un-sellable regardless of how good the engine is. **EPIC-27 is now the top priority:**
  a dependency-free Node-stdlib web front-door (open page → drag 3 files → see balances tie out → download the
  audit packet) over the existing engine. This is what turns "a tool I run in a terminal" into "a product a
  broker can use." After EPIC-27, resume hardening only as needed. Stack unchanged; no crypto; hosting stays a
  human deploy step (needs-human). Prefer EPIC-27 tasks over remaining EPIC-26 backend docs.

- **2026-06-24 — Strategist: STAGNATION BROKEN BY CONNECTING THE TWO HALVES OF THE PROJECT — stop shipping a
  FIFTH consecutive TrustLedger ENGINE increment around the SAME P-5 dam, and open EPIC-26 "tamper-evident
  reconciliation SEAL": reuse the project's ORIGINAL provenance core (`cli/core/manifest.js` + `attestation.js`,
  already built + tested) to turn the LEAD product's audit packet from an unsealed printout into a defensible,
  independently-verifiable evidentiary artifact.** No pivot; no stack change (still plain Node JS under
  `trustledger/`, reusing the existing `cli/core/` modules; Mocha tests under the unchanged `npx hardhat test`).
  - **Stagnation read (acted on, not recited).** Build frontier EMPTY — EPIC-22..25 all VERIFIED, 1398 tests
    green; the only open TODOs are the human-gated EPIC-3/4 (D-2/deploy). The metrics REGRESSED, not just
    plateaued: avgUsefulness 4.0 → 3.75, minUsefulness 4 → 3, humanGated standing 3→4→3→3 across the last runs.
    The directive for flat-and-mediocre-WITH-persistent-humanGated: do NOT invent more incremental items in the
    same vein — change approach MATERIALLY toward a capability that unlocks NEW value, and do NOT re-sharpen an

  - **The gap I found (confirmed in code, not invented).** `vh trust reconcile --out <dir>` writes the audit-ready
    HTML + CSV packet a broker hands a state real-estate examiner months later — but that packet is NOT
    tamper-evident. Nothing lets the examiner (or the broker defending themselves) prove "this is the EXACT packet
    TrustLedger produced on date T from these EXACT source files, byte-for-byte unaltered." `trustledger/close.js`
    has an `inputsDigest`, but its own NatSpec says it is a SHA-256 over the close's SUMMARY only — "NOT a
    cryptographic proof of the underlying source files." So the LEAD product's headline deliverable — a defensible
    audit artifact for a custodian carrying personal license risk — currently ships as an UNSEALED printout anyone
    can edit after the fact with nothing to detect it. That is precisely the evidentiary gap the provenance core
    was built to close.
  - **The move (the proven manifest/attestation pattern, repointed at the packet).** Reuse the EXISTING, tested
    `cli/core/manifest.js` (content-addressed manifest over a file set) + `attestation.js` (canonical unsigned
    attestation + offline verifier) VERBATIM — NO new crypto, NO contract change, NO network, NO key, NO new human
    decision — to bind {the three SOURCE inputs + every emitted packet file} into one content-addressed SEAL an
    examiner verifies OFFLINE. T-26.1 ships a PURE `trustledger/seal.js` (build/validate/verifySeal over
    already-loaded `{relPath,bytes}` entries, reusing manifest.js's hashing convention; per-file
    MATCH/CHANGED/MISSING/UNEXPECTED localization; OPTIONALLY wrappable in the shared signed-attestation envelope,
    proven with EPHEMERAL `Wallet.createRandom()` keys). T-26.2 wires `vh trust reconcile … --seal` (emit the seal
    after the packet; `--seal` without `--out` hard-errors) + a read-only OFFLINE `vh trust verify-seal <seal>`
    (0/3/2/1 exit, names exactly which file changed). T-26.3 documents it and SHARPENS P-5 #1 to note the
    deliverable is now a SEALED, independently-verifiable artifact (the CPA reviews a tamper-evident packet).
  - **Honest posture inherited verbatim.** The seal proves the inputs + packet are byte-for-byte what TrustLedger
    produced (TAMPER-EVIDENCE); "sealed ON date T" still rides the human-owned trust-root (P-3's signing/timestamp
    leg) and the seal SAYS so and references (does NOT execute) the human-gated sign/timestamp steps; it does NOT
    validate the legal MEANING of the reconciliation (the CPA review still governs). The seal is an UNTRUSTED
    transport container — verification RE-DERIVES, it does not trust the file's claims.
  - **Why this is genuinely higher-leverage than another increment.** EVERY P-5 sales path ends with a broker
    handing an examiner the audit packet and having to STAND BEHIND it. A reconciliation whose entire value is
    being a defensible audit record but which any text editor can silently alter is a printout, not evidence.
    Making the packet a sealed, independently-verifiable artifact is a NEW capability (defensibility) that connects
    the project's two halves — the provenance/verification core and the LEAD income product — and directly raises
    the deliverable's worth to the exact buyer. It is fully auto-buildable on already-tested core modules, with the
    test gate intact, and it does NOT touch any P-5 human gate.
  - **Why this beats the alternatives I considered.** (a) A fifth TrustLedger engine increment is the capped vein
    the regression warns against — four in a row plateaued then regressed. (b) Re-sharpening P-5 #1/#2/#3 is
    busywork; they are decision-ready. (c) Multi-period carry-forward of OUTSTANDING items is real breadth but is
    more engine work in the same vein and presupposes the packet is trustworthy. (d) A web/upload UI is premature
    (needs hosting, a human step). (e) Returning to DataLedger/ProofParcel is the vein the operator pivoted the
    lead AWAY from. The seal is the one auto-buildable thing that adds a NEW kind of value to the LEAD product
    while reusing the core the project already paid to build and test.
  - **Guardrails respected.** Pure-local, OFFLINE, deterministic, NO crypto/token/coin/NFT/sale/yield, NO funds,
    NO deploy, NO real key (only ephemeral `Wallet.createRandom()` test keys). No new dependency (reuses

    meaning and P-5 stays human-gated.

    coverage drawn from the real exports the target buyer uses. T-25.4 documents it and SHARPENS P-5 #3 so the

- **2026-06-24 — Strategist: BREAK THE VALUE CEILING by UNBLOCKING THE LEAD PRODUCT'S LAST live human blocker —
  open EPIC-24 "TrustLedger: period-close continuity." Turn the one-shot demo into the RECURRING monthly product
  P-5 #3 requires a design partner to keep using, the auto-buildable work that DE-RISKS / DIRECTLY UNBLOCKS the
  one remaining unsharpened item in P-5.** No pivot; no stack change (still plain Node JS under `trustledger/`,
  Mocha tests under the unchanged `npx hardhat test`).
  - **Plateau + value-ceiling read (acted on, not recited).** Build frontier EMPTY — EPIC-22 (TrustLedger v1)
    AND EPIC-23 (the per-state policy layer) are all VERIFIED. The last SIX metrics lines are a hard ceiling:
    avgUsefulness FLAT at 4, minUsefulness stuck at 4, humanGated standing 3→3→4→3→4→3. The directive: when
    quality plateaus AND humanGated persists, do NOT invent more increments in the capped vein — SHARPEN the
    blocking needs-human proposal and BUILD the auto-buildable work that de-risks / directly unblocks it. The dam
    is P-5 (TrustLedger go-to-market). EPIC-23 already sharpened P-5 #2 (per-state policy → a fill-in-the-table
    handoff). The remaining LIVE, unsharpened blocker is P-5 #3: a human must get 1–2 design partners to run their
    REAL MONTHLY files and confirm the tie-out. I did NOT re-sharpen P-5 #1/#2 (CPA sign-off and the policy table
    are already decision-ready human asks) — I attacked the one item that still de-risks with buildable work.
  - **The gap I found (confirmed against the code, not invented).** A trust reconciliation is a CONTINUOUS monthly
    chain: month N's ENDING bank/book balances ARE month N+1's OPENING balances, and that equality is the audit
    trail an examiner walks down the months. I surveyed the engine: `reconcile.js` accepts `opts.opening` and
    `cli.js` exposes `--opening-bank`/`--opening-book` as RAW numbers the broker re-types BY HAND every month.
    There is (a) NO machine-readable artifact a run emits that the next run can consume as its opening, and (b) NO
    continuity check whatsoever — a fat-fingered opening silently shifts every balance and can flip PASS↔FAIL with
    no warning. The packet computes `balances.reconciled` (the ending number) but never exposes a structured close,
    and the next run has no way to assert "my opening == the prior period's ending." The single most error-prone,
    most-repeated step of the legally-forced monthly chore is unguarded — and it bites EXACTLY on month two, the
    moment a design partner decides whether this is a real recurring product or a one-off toy.
  - **The move (the proven receipt/policy pattern, applied to the period chain).** EPIC-6 shipped a versioned,
    strictly-validated receipt artifact; EPIC-23 shipped a versioned, strictly-validated policy. EPIC-24 does the
    identical thing for the period chain: T-24.1 ships `trustledger/close.js` (a versioned, strictly-validated
    `*.close.json` carrying period/reportDate/opening/ending/subledger/pass + a SHA-256 inputs digest, built PURELY
    from the existing packet model + a pure `checkContinuity`); T-24.2 wires `--prior-close`/`--emit-close` into
    `vh trust reconcile` so a run SEEDS its opening from the prior close AND raises a hard new `CONTINUITY_BREAK`
    (error, policy-overridable) when the roll-forward is not penny-exact, flowing through the SAME PASS/exit/report
    path; T-24.3 documents it and SHARPENS P-5 #3 from "engage partners and run their files" to the concrete,
    decision-ready design-partner SCRIPT: "run month 1 with `--emit-close`, run month 2 with `--prior-close`,
    confirm both months tie out AND the roll-forward is clean — that two-month run IS the WTP validation."
  - **Why this is genuinely higher-leverage than another increment.** A reconciler that only does ONE month is a
    demo, not a product — the value of a trust-reconciliation tool is that it runs EVERY month with the chain proven
    forward, and the chief footgun (a mis-typed opening that silently changes PASS) is exactly what an unguarded
    one-shot leaves open. Making the period chain a machine-emitted, continuity-checked artifact is the precondition
    for a design partner to use it past month one — which is what P-5 #3 actually validates. That is a NEW capability
    for the LEAD income product (recurring, auditable continuity), not polish, and it directly removes the friction
    between "a broker tried it once" and "a broker runs it as their monthly close."
  - **Why this beats the alternatives I considered.** (a) Another DataLedger/ProofParcel/provenance increment is the
    capped vein the plateau warns against and the human pivoted the lead AWAY from. (b) Multi-period / carry-forward
    of OUTSTANDING items (a check that stays outstanding across months) is real future value but is feature-breadth,
    not the P-5 blocker — and it sits naturally ON TOP of the close artifact this EPIC introduces, so this is the
    right first layer. (c) A web upload UI is premature (needs hosting, a human step) and doesn't touch the
    recurring-use gap. (d) P-5 #1/#2 are already sharp human asks; re-sharpening them is busywork. The period-close
    continuity layer is the one auto-buildable thing that directly de-risks the LEAD product's last live human gate.
  - **Guardrails respected.** Pure-local, offline, deterministic, NO crypto/token/coin/NFT/sale/yield, NO funds, NO
    deploy, NO real key. No new heavy dependency (a small pure JSON close module; SHA-256 via Node's built-in
    `crypto`; no PDF/xlsx libs). ADDITIVE: with no `--prior-close`/`--emit-close` the engine behaves byte-for-byte as
    today, so every EPIC-22/23 test stays green and the test COMMAND is unchanged. REVENUE INTEGRITY unchanged: income
    = a SaaS subscription for a legally-forced monthly chore from paying brokers — the CPA/counsel review, per-state
    policy sign-off, the design partners, hosting, pricing, and billing all stay human steps (P-5). The close artifact
    is an UNTRUSTED convenience hint (re-derive; not signed/timestamped); the loop ships only the FORMAT + the
    validated continuity check, and must NOT auto-resolve any legal meaning.

- **2026-06-24 — Strategist: BREAK THE VALUE CEILING by UNBLOCKING THE LEAD PRODUCT'S real blocker — open
  EPIC-23 "TrustLedger: the per-state trust-rule POLICY layer." Turn the hard-coded exception severities into a
  reviewed, citable, data-driven control, the auto-buildable work that DE-RISKS / DIRECTLY UNBLOCKS P-5 item #2.**
  No pivot; no stack change (still plain Node JS under `trustledger/`, Mocha tests under the unchanged
  `npx hardhat test`).
  - **Plateau + value-ceiling read (acted on, not recited).** Build frontier EMPTY — EPIC-22 (TrustLedger v1:
    ingest → match → reconcile → report + the one-command `vh trust reconcile`) all VERIFIED, 1178 tests green; the
    only open TODOs are the human-gated D-2/deploy items. The last SIX metrics lines are a hard ceiling:
    avgUsefulness FLAT at 4, minUsefulness stuck at 4, humanGated standing 3→3→4→3→4→3. The directive: when quality
    plateaus AND humanGated persists, do NOT invent more increments in the capped vein — SHARPEN the blocking
    needs-human proposal and BUILD the auto-buildable work that de-risks / directly unblocks it. For the new LEAD
    product the dam is P-5 (TrustLedger go-to-market).
  - **The gap I found (confirmed against the code, not invented).** I surveyed the engine: PASS is decided by
    `report.js` › `buildPacket` as `pass = rec.tiesOut && counts.error === 0`, so the verdict hinges ENTIRELY on
    which exceptions are ERROR vs WARNING. That mapping is the HARD-CODED `DEFAULT_SEVERITY` table in
    `reconcile.js` (security-deposit-not-segregated = ERROR, NSF = WARNING, owner draw = WARNING, …). P-5 item #2
    flags exactly this: those severities are STATE-DEPENDENT LAW shipped as if settled, and a human must "produce a
    documented, citable per-state mapping that REPLACES the hard-coded severities." But there is NO mechanism to
    plug a reviewed mapping IN — the human would have to edit source, and the meaning of PASS would silently change
    under them. The reviewed control the buyer's auditor actually relies on cannot exist until the policy is DATA,
    not code.
  - **The move (the proven EPIC-16 pattern, applied to the LEAD product).** EPIC-16 turned DataLedger from a tool
    that DESCRIBED license provenance into one that GATED it against a versioned, validated policy FILE. EPIC-23
    does the identical thing for TrustLedger's severities: T-23.1 ships `trustledger/policy.js` (a versioned,
    strictly-validated per-state policy + a pure `applyPolicy` that overrides severities, built on the EXISTING
    `EXCEPTION`/`SEVERITY` enums so a typo'd type is a hard error) + sample DRAFT policy fixtures; T-23.2 wires
    `--state`/`--policy` into `vh trust reconcile` so the PASS verdict + exit code reflect the REVIEWED policy and
    the report names the governing policy + surfaces each override's citation; T-23.3 documents it and SHARPENS
    P-5 #2 from "rewrite the engine's classification" to the now-narrow human task "fill in + have counsel sign the
    per-state policy TABLE in the shipped, validated format — the engine already consumes it."
  - **Why this is genuinely higher-leverage than another increment.** A correct engine that hard-codes
    state-dependent law as settled is NOT a sellable compliance control — its PASS is the loop's draft opinion, not
    a defensible per-state determination. Making the policy a reviewed, citable, swappable artifact is the exact
    bridge that converts P-5 #2 from a from-scratch legal/engineering task into a fill-in-the-table handoff, and it
    is what an auditor's checklist and a CPA's sign-off actually attach to. That is a NEW capability for the LEAD
    income product, not polish, and it directly removes the biggest piece of friction between "correct engine" and
    "sellable control."
  - **Why this beats the alternatives I considered.** (a) Another DataLedger/ProofParcel/provenance increment is
    the capped vein the plateau warns against and re-caps at 4 (and the human pivoted the lead AWAY from it).
    (b) Multi-period / carry-forward reconciliation is real value but is feature-breadth, not the P-5 blocker — it
    can wait. (c) A web upload UI is premature (needs hosting, a human step) and doesn't touch the compliance-control
    gap. (d) P-1/P-2 (crypto/deploy) are human-only. The per-state policy layer is the one auto-buildable thing that
    directly de-risks the LEAD product's actual value ceiling.
  - **Guardrails respected.** Pure-local, offline, deterministic, NO crypto/token/coin/NFT/sale/yield, NO funds, NO
    deploy, NO real key. No new heavy dependency (a small pure JSON policy module; no PDF/xlsx libs). ADDITIVE: with
    no `--policy`/`--state` the engine behaves byte-for-byte as today (the existing defaults become the built-in
    baseline policy), so every EPIC-22 test stays green and the test COMMAND is unchanged. REVENUE INTEGRITY
    unchanged: income = a SaaS subscription for a legally-forced monthly chore from paying brokers — the CPA/counsel
    review of the policy, per-state research, hosting, pricing, billing, and design partners all stay human steps
    (P-5). The loop ships only the FORMAT + the validated engine + the draft fixtures a human reviews; it must NOT
    auto-resolve the legal meaning of any severity.

- **2026-06-24 — Builder: T-22.4 SHIPPED — the demoable TrustLedger core: `vh trust reconcile <bank>
  <ledger> <rentroll> [--out <dir>]`.** One command runs the whole pipeline end-to-end (ingest → match →
  reconcile → report) and writes a DATED, deterministic, audit-ready packet as **HTML + CSV** into the
  caller-chosen `--out` directory (created if absent; NEVER cwd; without `--out` it prints the summary +
  HTML to stdout and writes nothing), plus a one-line PASS/FAIL summary and a CI-gateable exit code
  (0 PASS / 3 FAIL=does-not-tie-out-or-out-of-trust / 2 usage / 1 IO). HTML is print-to-PDF-ready and CSV
  opens in any spreadsheet, so binary PDF/xlsx libs are deferred to v2 (no new heavy deps). The packet leads
  with a prominent disclaimer: the tool AIDS reconciliation; the broker remains the responsible custodian.
  Test command unchanged: `npx hardhat test`.
  - **Files.** `trustledger/report.js` (pure, I/O-free packet model + HTML/CSV renderers; takes an explicit
    report date — no hidden clock — so output is byte-reproducible), `trustledger/cli.js` (`runReconcile` +
    `vh trust reconcile` dispatch, injectable IO/today for deterministic tests), wired into `cli/vh.js`
    (`vh trust` case + usage). E2E: `test/trustledger.e2e.test.js` drives the public command over a fixture
    set (`trustledger/fixtures/e2e/`) and asserts the three balances, the exception list, determinism, exit
    codes, and that every filesystem effect is isolated to a throwaway temp dir (no leaked artifacts). Suite
    green (1178 passing).

- **2026-06-24 — OPERATOR DIRECTION (from the human): NEW LEAD PRODUCT = TrustLedger.** A focused multi-agent
  market study (15 ideas generated + scored) chose TrustLedger as the strongest *income* bet, and the human
  confirmed it ("just pick the best, we can always do more later"). The provenance line (DataLedger/ProofParcel)
  is now MATURE (installable package, runnable buyer example, timestamp/attestation legs) — keep it green, but
  the **primary build focus shifts to EPIC-22 (TrustLedger)** as the new top of the backlog.
  - **What it is.** Automated three-way **trust-account reconciliation** for small US residential property-
    management firms (~50–500 doors) that run on QuickBooks + a bank CSV + a rent ledger (NOT on AppFolio/
    Buildium). Upload three files they already have monthly → match transactions (exact + fuzzy) → compute the
    three balances that must legally agree (bank vs book vs tenant sub-ledgers) → flag every exception → emit a
    dated, audit-ready reconciliation packet. The broker is the legal trust-account custodian and carries
    personal license risk, so willingness-to-pay is high; reachable purely via high-intent SEO/ads/NARPM forums.
  - **Why it scored highest.** Fully buildable + locally testable as a DETERMINISTIC parser/matcher/reporter
    (no LLM-accuracy gamble), tied to a legally-forced recurring chore, reachable with zero insider network.
  - **Stack: NO change.** Plain Node JS modules + Mocha tests under the existing `npx hardhat test` command
    (the test runner is Mocha-via-hardhat). New code lives under `trustledger/`; tests under `test/`.
  - **REVENUE INTEGRITY unchanged:** income = SaaS subscription from paying customers; NO token/coin. The loop
    BUILDS the engine + report + (later) a thin web UI; the human owns hosting, Stripe, a CPA review of the
    report format + disclaimer, per-state trust-rule research, and the design-partner brokers (needs-human).

- **2026-06-24 — Strategist: BREAK THE PLATEAU BY CHANGING THE KIND OF WORK — stop building trust-root
  variations (that vein is EXHAUSTED) and MAKE THE PRODUCT ACTUALLY INSTALLABLE: open EPIC-21 "the `vh`
  command a paying customer can run." The product is currently NON-INSTALLABLE and CRASHES when published.**
  No pivot in product; no stack change (still Node CLI + Solidity, test command unchanged: `npx hardhat
  test`). This is a deliberate change of WORK KIND — packaging/distribution + a runnable demo — away from the
  capped trust-root vein, per the stagnation directive.
  - **Plateau + value-ceiling read (acted on, not recited).** Frontier EMPTY (EPIC-13..20 all VERIFIED,
    1066+ tests green; only open TODOs are D-2/deploy needs-decision items). The last FIVE metrics lines are a
    hard ceiling: avgUsefulness FLAT at 4.0, minUsefulness stuck at 4, humanGated standing 3→3→3→4→3. The
    directive: when quality plateaus AND humanGated persists, do NOT invent more increments in the capped
    vein — change approach MATERIALLY (a capability that unlocks new value, or remove what isn't paying off)
    AND sharpen/de-risk the human blocker.
  - **Why the trust-root vein is DONE (so more of it is the capped work).** EPIC-15/17/19 fully shipped P-3
    Option A (canonical unsigned payload → signed-container format → offline verifier → the one-command
    `vh dataset/parcel sign`). EPIC-20 fully shipped P-3 Option B (RFC-3161 request-digest → wrap container →
    offline `verify-timestamp`). BOTH options are collapsed in P-3 to "provision/obtain, run one command."
    Option C is on-chain-anchor — that's a deploy + real funds, human-gated (P-2). There is no auto-buildable
    trust-root work left that isn't a third polish of the same idea, which is exactly what re-caps usefulness
    at 4. I did NOT re-sharpen P-3 again: P-1 (D-2) and P-3 (Options A/B) are ALREADY exhaustively
    decision-ready — the dam is a human ACTION, not missing design. More design de-risking would be busywork.
  - **The materially-different, higher-leverage gap I found (confirmed in code, not assumed).** I surveyed
    package.json + cli/ and found a foundational, overlooked defect: THE PRODUCT IS NOT INSTALLABLE and is
    BROKEN when published. (1) package.json declares NO `bin`, so `npm install -g verifyhash && vh ...` — the
    EXACT UX every doc/README/in-band help documents — produces no `vh` command; the only way to run it is
    `node cli/vh.js` from a git checkout. (2) `ethers` is required in 34 places across cli/ but is NOT a
    declared dependency — it resolves ONLY transitively via the `@nomicfoundation/hardhat-toolbox` DEV dep, so
    `npm install verifyhash` ships a package that CRASHES with `Cannot find module 'ethers'` on first use. (3)
    No `files` allowlist / no `engines`. This is the difference between "40 internal scripts that only run
    from a git checkout" and "a product a paying customer can install and run as documented."
  - **Why this is genuinely higher-leverage than another verifier increment.** EVERY monetization path in
    P-3/P-4 (a design-partner evaluation, an on-prem license, a metered pipeline) STARTS with the buyer
    installing the tool and running `vh`. No amount of trust-root polish matters if `npm install` crashes and
    the documented command doesn't exist. Fixing install + shipping a runnable, self-checking end-to-end
    example is the prerequisite that makes all eight shipped EPICs reachable by a paying customer — and it
    directly de-risks the human GTM steps (you cannot hand a design partner a CLI that isn't packaged).
  - **Shape.** T-21.1 makes `vh` a real installable command (declare `bin`, move `ethers` to real
    `dependencies`, add a `files` allowlist + `engines`), gated by a NEW pure packaging-integrity test that
    fails if any cli/ runtime `require` of a bare module is undeclared (so this class of defect can never
    silently return). T-21.2 ships `examples/` — committed sample data + ONE runnable, offline, no-key script
    that drives the real DataLedger + ProofParcel pipeline end to end — gated by a test that runs it, asserts
    a policy violation is flagged and a tamper is caught, and proves it leaves the working tree clean.
  - **Honest posture inherited.** The example demonstrates tamper-evidence + the unsigned attestation bytes
    only; "unaltered since date T" still rides the human-owned trust-root (P-3), and the script SAYS so and
    references (does NOT execute) the human-gated sign/timestamp/anchor steps. README's install note documents
    the LOCAL install path (`npm install -g .` / `npm link`); PUBLISHING to the npm registry is an outward
    action and stays a human step (noted as such, not auto-run).
  - **Why this beats the alternatives.** (a) A third trust-root variation is the capped vein the plateau warns
    against. (b) EPIC-3 reputation is BLOCKED on D-2 (P-1, human-only). (c) More descriptive DataLedger/
    ProofParcel polish re-caps at 4. Installability + a living demo is a NEW kind of value (the product
    becomes actually adoptable), fully auto-buildable, with the test gate intact.
  - **Guardrails respected.** Pure-local, offline, no funds, no deploy, no real key, no token framing — nothing
    touches D-2/EPIC-3/EPIC-4 or REVENUE INTEGRITY (income comes from selling the product to paying customers,
    a HUMAN step). No contract change. No NEW dependency — T-21.1 only makes the ALREADY-USED `ethers`
    explicit and the example uses only existing modules. Publishing to npm and all sales/pricing stay
    human-gated. All existing commands and tests stay byte-for-byte green; the test COMMAND is unchanged.

- **2026-06-23 — Strategist: BREAK THE VALUE CEILING by BUILDING THE UNBUILT HALF OF THE SAME BLOCKER —
  open EPIC-20 "Independent timestamp proof: the RFC-3161 envelope + offline verifier" (P-3 Option B). This
  is the EPIC-17 move applied to the TIMESTAMP dimension instead of the SIGNATURE dimension, NOT another
  descriptive increment.** No pivot; no stack change (still Node CLI + Solidity, test command unchanged:
  `npx hardhat test`).
  - **Value-ceiling read (acted on, not recited).** Frontier EMPTY (EPIC-13..19 all VERIFIED, 1166+ tests
    green; only open TODOs are D-2-blocked needs-decision items). The last FIVE metrics lines are a hard
    ceiling: avgUsefulness FLAT at 4.0, minUsefulness stuck at 4, `humanGated` standing 3→4→3 with no upward
    movement. The directive: a persistent humanGated count is a VALUE CEILING — SHARPEN the blocking proposal
    AND build the auto-buildable work that DE-RISKS / DIRECTLY UNBLOCKS the real value; do NOT invent more
    increments in the capped vein. The dam is P-3 (the signing/TIMESTAMP trust-root).
  - **Why NOT more signature/sign work, and why this is genuinely higher-leverage.** EPIC-15/17/19 already
    EXHAUSTIVELY built P-3's SIGNATURE dimension (Option A): canonical UNSIGNED payload, signed-container
    FORMAT, offline verifier, AND the one-command `vh dataset/parcel sign`. But Option A is the HONESTLY-WEAK
    trust-root — a self-managed signature attests only "the publisher SAYS SO," NOT a trusted TIMESTAMP. The
    SINGLE most-repeated limitation in the whole product (docs/DATALEDGER.md, every TRUST_NOTE, P-3's own
    text) is "a manifest is NOT a timestamp — it cannot make the 'unaltered since date T' claim an EU-AI-Act /
    due-diligence reviewer ultimately wants." P-3 names Option (B) — an INDEPENDENT RFC-3161 Timestamp
    Authority — as the enterprise upgrade that delivers that claim. I grepped all of cli/+docs/+test/: there
    is ZERO timestamp-token handling anywhere. So unlike the signature dimension (format + verifier both
    shipped), the TIMESTAMP dimension has NEITHER — and it is the half that carries the actual buyer-relevant
    claim. Building it is materially higher-leverage than any further Option-A polish.
  - **The guardrail-safe insight (EPIC-17's, applied to the timestamp).** The loop must NEVER obtain a real
    timestamp token — that requires an outward network request to a real TSA (a human-owned, possibly paid
    relationship), so OBTAINING a token stays human-gated, exactly like PROVISIONING a key did. But the loop
    CAN, with NO network and NO new trust it holds: (1) DEFINE the detached `*-attestation-timestamped`
    container that WRAPS the exact canonical-attestation digest + the RFC-3161 token (wrap-don't-edit, same
    invariant as the signed envelope), and (2) build an OFFLINE VERIFIER that parses the token's `TSTInfo`,
    confirms its `messageImprint` binds EXACTLY the buyer's own canonical-attestation digest, and reports the
    asserted `genTime` / TSA serial / policy OID — proved end-to-end with SELF-MINTED throwaway TEST tokens (a
    test-only mock TSA with an ephemeral key, the timestamp analogue of `Wallet.createRandom()`). This
    converts P-3 Option (B)'s handoff from "design an envelope AND obtain a token AND build a verifier" to
    purely "obtain a token from your TSA over the digest `timestamp-request` emits, `timestamp-wrap` it, DONE
    — buyers verify offline with `verify-timestamp`."
  - **Shape.** T-20.1 adds a small PURE dependency-free RFC-3161 DER reader (`cli/core/rfc3161.js`) +
    `bindsDigest`, proved with a test-only minted token. T-20.2 adds the detached timestamp-container engine
    (sibling of attestation.js) + `vh dataset/parcel timestamp-request` (emit the digest your TSA stamps) and
    `timestamp-wrap` (wrap the returned token). T-20.3 ships `vh dataset/parcel verify-timestamp` (OFFLINE,
    no key, no network, 0/3 exit, `--manifest` binds to the buyer's data), docs, and SHARPENS P-3 Option (B)
    to the four-step handoff.
  - **Honest, bounded posture (never overclaims).** The verifier proves the binding + surfaces the asserted
    genTime but does NOT validate the TSA's X.509 certificate CHAIN — that is the human trust anchor (you
    TRUST your chosen TSA's published cert), exactly mirroring how Option A pins the signer ADDRESS. In-band
    output says so and points to a CMS verifier / `openssl ts -verify` for full PKI validation. Even so this
    is materially stronger than Option A: an INDEPENDENT third party (not the publisher) attests existence by
    genTime.
  - **Why this beats the alternatives.** (a) Another DataLedger/ProofParcel descriptive increment is the
    capped vein the plateau warns against. (b) EPIC-3 reputation is BLOCKED on D-2 (P-1, human-only). (c) More
    signature/`sign`/P-3-prose work is DONE — Option A is fully shipped. Option B is the UNBUILT half of the
    SAME blocker and the one a paying buyer actually pays for; its format + offline verifier is the exact
    de-risking the value-ceiling directive asks for, on the shared core, for BOTH products. A genuinely NEW
    capability (independent timestamp proof), not polish.
  - **Guardrails respected.** Pure-local, OFFLINE, no funds, no deploy, no real key, no real TSA, no token
    framing — nothing touches D-2/EPIC-3/EPIC-4 or REVENUE INTEGRITY (income comes from selling the product to
    paying customers, a HUMAN step). No contract change. The loop NEVER calls a TSA, holds no token, generates
    none; the only tokens in tests are self-minted throwaway TEST tokens (mock TSA, ephemeral key, NO real
    funds). No new dependency (a small pure bounded DER reader; ethers already present), no global install, no
    network. The UNSIGNED attest, signed-attest, sign, and verify-attest paths and ALL their tests stay
    byte-for-byte green (timestamp wrapping is purely additive). P-3 Option (B) stays human-gated (obtain the
    token from a real TSA); EPIC-20 ships only the request-digest, the wrap container, and the offline verifier.

- **2026-06-23 — Strategist: BREAK THE VALUE CEILING by BUILDING THE HUMAN'S MISSING SIGNING LEG — open
  EPIC-19 "`vh sign`: the one-command signing leg" — the last auto-buildable mile of P-3/P-4, NOT another
  descriptive increment.** No pivot; no stack change (still Node CLI + Solidity, test command unchanged:
  `npx hardhat test`).
  - **Value-ceiling read (acted on, not recited).** Frontier EMPTY (EPIC-13..18 all VERIFIED, 1166 tests green;
    the only open TODOs are D-2-blocked needs-decision items). Last metrics are a hard ceiling: avgUsefulness
    FLAT at 4.0, minUsefulness stuck at 4, and `humanGated` GROWING 3→3→3→4. The directive is explicit — a
    persistent/growing humanGated count is a VALUE CEILING; do NOT invent more incremental tasks in the capped
    vein. SHARPEN the blocking proposal AND build the auto-buildable work that DE-RISKS / DIRECTLY UNBLOCKS the
    real value once the human acts. The dam is P-3 (the signing/timestamp trust-root — the income product's
    biggest unlock, shared by BOTH products and named in P-4 for ProofParcel).
  - **The gap I found (confirmed against the code, not invented).** EPIC-17 collapsed P-3's DESIGN to nothing:
    the loop ships the canonical UNSIGNED payload (`vh dataset/parcel attest`), the signed-container FORMAT
    (cli/core/attestation.js `buildSignedAttestation`), and the OFFLINE verifier (`verify-attest`). But I
    surveyed cli/core/attestation.js and grepped all of cli/ — there is NO command that takes a key and PRODUCES
    the signed container. `buildSignedAttestation` (attestation.js:188) accepts an already-computed `signature`
    STRING; `recoverSigner` (attestation.js:279) verifies an `eip191-personal-sign` signature over the embedded
    canonical bytes; but the ONLY thing that ever CREATES such a signature is the ephemeral
    `Wallet.createRandom()` keys inside the tests. So a real publisher who has provisioned a key must hand-craft
    the EIP-191 signature with EXTERNAL tooling and hand-assemble the container JSON — exactly the bytes one
    command should produce. That manual, error-prone step is the last auto-buildable mile of P-3/P-4's revenue
    path, and it is what the humanGated ceiling is actually damming for the self-managed-key (Option A) pilot.
  - **The guardrail-safe insight (EPIC-17's, applied to the signer).** The loop must NEVER provision, generate,
    hold, or persist a real key — but it CAN build a `sign` command that READS a key the HUMAN supplies at
    runtime (`--key-env <VAR>` or `--key-file <path>` the human created OUTSIDE the loop), uses it in-process
    ONLY to sign the canonical bytes, and NEVER writes/logs/echoes it. The loop holds no key of its own and
    generates none; the only keys anywhere in repo/tests stay EPHEMERAL throwaway `Wallet.createRandom()`
    test-only keys (NEVER a real-funds key) — identical to the EPIC-17 verify tests. ethers 6 (already a
    dependency) provides `Wallet.signMessage` (EIP-191 personal_sign) — no new dependency, no network.
  - **Shape.** T-19.1 adds a shared-core `signAttestation({ attestation, signer }, cfg)` (re-validate +
    serialize the canonical bytes, `await signer.signMessage(bytes)`, then call the EXISTING
    `buildSignedAttestation` — so the container goes through the validated path and round-trips with
    `recoverSigner`/`verifySignedAttestation`), proven with ephemeral keys for BOTH the dataset and parcel cfgs.
    T-19.2 ships `vh dataset sign` + `vh parcel sign --key-env <VAR>|--key-file <path> [--out] [--json]`: build
    the UNSIGNED payload exactly as `attest` does, construct an ethers Wallet from the human-supplied key, sign,
    write the container the existing `verify-attest` accepts; the key is read-used-discarded, output prints ONLY
    the public signer address + path + scheme, and neither/both/missing/malformed key sources hard-error WITHOUT
    leaking the key. T-19.3 documents it and SHARPENS P-3/P-4 so Option (A)'s handoff collapses to "provision a
    key, run `vh dataset/parcel sign --key-env`, DONE."
  - **Honest posture inherited verbatim.** A self-managed-key signature attests the dataset/parcel IDENTITY +
    "the signer says so" — it is NOT a trusted TIMESTAMP; "unaltered since date T" still rides the human-owned
    trust-root P-3 (or the stronger B/C options). The `sign` command says so in-band and never overclaims.
  - **Why this beats the alternatives.** (a) Another DataLedger/ProofParcel descriptive increment is the capped
    vein the plateau warns against and re-caps at 4. (b) EPIC-3 reputation is BLOCKED on D-2 (P-1, human-only).
    (c) More P-3 PROSE-sharpening alone is done — it is provision-only — but the loop CAN build the command the
    human runs AFTER provisioning, which is the exact de-risking work the directive asks for. A `sign` command
    is a NEW capability removing the single biggest remaining piece of manual friction between "a human has a
    key" and "a paying buyer can verify a signed attestation," for BOTH products on the shared core.
  - **Guardrails respected.** Pure-local, offline, no funds, no deploy, no real key, no token framing — nothing
    touches D-2/EPIC-3/EPIC-4 or REVENUE INTEGRITY (no token/coin/NFT/sale/airdrop/staking; income comes from
    selling the product to paying customers, a HUMAN step). No contract change. The loop NEVER
    provisions/generates/holds/persists a real key; the key is read from a human-supplied source at runtime, used
    only to sign, never written or logged. The UNSIGNED attest + verify-attest paths and ALL their tests stay
    byte-for-byte green (sign is purely additive). Only ephemeral `Wallet.createRandom()` test keys appear. No
    new dependency, no global install, no network. P-3/P-4 stay human-gated (provision the key + GTM/legal);
    EPIC-19 ships only the command the human runs locally with a key they alone provisioned.

  - **Value-ceiling read (per the directive, acted on — not recited).** The build frontier is EMPTY (EPIC-13..17

  - **Why I did NOT just sharpen P-3 again.** I sharpen the blocker when it is dull. P-3 is the OPPOSITE — it has
    been sharpened EXHAUSTIVELY across EPIC-15 (the canonical UNSIGNED payload `vh dataset attest`) and EPIC-17
    (the signed-attestation envelope + the offline `vh dataset verify-attest`, proved end-to-end with EPHEMERAL
    throwaway keys). I re-read P-3 (STRATEGY.md:1201-1244): it is already collapsed to PROVISION-ONLY for Option
    (A) — "pick A/B/C; provision a real key (NEVER inside the loop) and sign the canonical bytes with the
    documented scheme." There is NO design left for the loop to do and the loop CANNOT provision a real key. So

    capped vein that re-caps usefulness at 4. The directive's other prong applies: pursue a HIGHER-LEVERAGE

  - **The move (the operator pivot's own promise, never started).** The 2026-06-23 OPERATOR DIRECTION said
    plainly: "DataLedger, ProofParcel (B2B data-delivery receipts), AttestKit (SOC2/ISO audit-log evidence) all
    sit on the SAME core. After DataLedger v1 lands, expand into these as THIN product adapters over the shared
    engine — one core, many paying buyers." DataLedger has now landed v1 → v1.4; the family expansion is overdue.
    ProofParcel targets a DIFFERENT paying buyer with a DIFFERENT budgeted reason to pay: B2B data exchange where
    a delivery dispute ("you never sent file X" / "the file you sent was altered") is expensive, so a contractual
    PROOF-OF-DELIVERY receipt — tamper-evident, signable, independently verifiable, pinning exactly which files
    (names + bytes) were delivered for which parcel between which parties — is worth paying for (data vendors,
    market-data redistributors, ML-data marketplaces, any contract with a delivery-acceptance clause).
  - **Why it's genuinely a THIN adapter (confirmed against the code, not assumed).** The provenance engine is
    ALREADY cleanly factored and reused: cli/hash.js exposes hashDirStream/pathLeaf/buildTree/proofForIndex;
    cli/proof.js exposes the portable proof-artifact machinery; cli/dataset.js is itself a thin consumer
    (require("./hash"), require("./proof")). ProofParcel reuses the IDENTICAL Merkle/manifest/proof/attest/
    verify-attest machinery repointed at a delivery context (parcelId/sender/recipient as UNTRUSTED hints) — NO
    new crypto, NO contract change, NO network, NO key, NO new human design decision. T-18.1 first EXTRACTS the
    manifest + signed-attestation machinery (currently inside dataset.js with "dataset" framing) into a clean,
    product-agnostic `cli/core/` library so BOTH products (and AttestKit later) depend on ONE tested
    implementation with ONE copy of the TRUST_NOTE caveats — a PURE refactor that keeps DataLedger byte-for-byte
    unchanged (dataset.js becomes a thin wrapper; all 859 tests pass). T-18.2 ships `vh parcel build/verify`;
    T-18.3 ships `vh parcel attest/verify-attest` on the SAME signed-attestation core + docs/PROOFPARCEL.md.
  - **Honest trust posture inherited, not overclaimed.** ProofParcel inherits P-3's posture VERBATIM: a parcel
    receipt binds the file SET to a root and is signable with the same envelope, but is NOT by itself a trusted
    delivery TIMESTAMP — "delivered ON date T" still rides the human-owned trust-root P-3. The loop ships only the
    FORMAT + the OFFLINE verifier; any signing in tests uses EPHEMERAL throwaway `Wallet.createRandom()` keys.
  - **Why this beats the alternatives I considered.** (a) Another DataLedger increment is the capped vein the
    plateau warns against and would re-cap at 4. (b) EPIC-3 reputation is BLOCKED on D-2 (P-1, human-only) and is
    a deprioritized crypto feature. (c) More P-3 de-risking is DONE — it is provision-only and the loop cannot
    hold a real key. A SECOND product on the shared core multiplies shots on goal with a NEW buyer, FORCES the
    core to become a real reusable library (de-risking the whole family — DataLedger + ProofParcel + the future
    AttestKit), and is fully auto-buildable with the existing test gate. Per the income guardrails, building more
    products multiplies shots on goal but does NOT itself produce revenue — landing a ProofParcel design-partner,
    pricing, and the signing trust-root remain HUMAN steps (P-3, and the new P-4 below).
  - **Guardrails respected.** Pure-local, offline, no funds, no deploy, no token framing — nothing here touches
    D-2/EPIC-3/EPIC-4 or REVENUE INTEGRITY (no token/coin/NFT/sale/airdrop/staking; income comes from selling the
    product to paying customers, a HUMAN step). No contract change; reuses the EXISTING offline core verbatim. The
    DataLedger commands and ALL their tests stay byte-for-byte green (the extraction re-exports from core). The
    signing trust-root stays human-gated (P-3); ProofParcel ships only the FORMAT + the OFFLINE verifier. No new
    dependency (ethers already present), no global install, no network. Added P-4 (ProofParcel go-to-market) to
    needs-human so the revenue step is explicitly a human action, not implied by the build.

- **2026-06-23 — Strategist: BREAK THE VALUE CEILING — open EPIC-17 "DataLedger v1.4: the signed-attestation
  envelope + offline verifier" — the auto-buildable work that DE-RISKS and DIRECTLY UNBLOCKS the persistent
  humanGated blocker P-3, instead of another descriptive increment in the capped vein.** No pivot; no stack
  change (still Node CLI + Solidity, test command unchanged: `npx hardhat test`).
  - **Plateau + value-ceiling read (per the directive, acted on — not recited).** The build frontier is EMPTY
    (EPIC-13..16 all VERIFIED, 800+ tests green) and the last THREE METRICS lines are a hard plateau:
    avgUsefulness flat at 4.0, minUsefulness stuck at 4, AND `humanGated: 3` STANDING across all three. The
    directive is explicit: a persistent humanGated count is a VALUE CEILING — the highest-leverage work is
    dammed behind an unresolved human decision and the loop is being forced into lower-leverage work around it.
    The correct response is NOT more incremental DataLedger description/report/check polish (the exact capped
    vein) — it is to SHARPEN the blocking proposal and BUILD the auto-buildable work that de-risks / directly
    unblocks it. The three needs-human proposals are P-1 (D-2 token framing — a crypto feature the income pivot
    deprioritized), P-2 (deploy), and P-3 (DataLedger signing/timestamp trust-root). P-3 is the INCOME
    product's single biggest unlock — it is what makes the "unaltered since date T" claim an EU-AI-Act /
    due-diligence reviewer ultimately wants — so it is the right blocker to attack.
  - **The gap I found (confirmed against the code, not invented).** The loop already built the part of P-3 it
    can do without the human decision: `vh dataset attest` (T-15.2) emits the deterministic, canonical UNSIGNED
    payload. But I surveyed cli/dataset.js (`validateAttestation` 1540-1584, `serializeAttestation` 1594-1609,
    `readAttestation`) and grepped all of cli/+test/ for signature primitives — the signing loop is HALF-built
    in a way that STILL blocks P-3 hard: (1) `validateAttestation` HARD-REJECTS any `signed:true`/non-null
    `signature`, and `serializeAttestation` has NO slot a real signature can ride in — so even after a human
    signs the bytes, there is no defined envelope to put the signature in (P-3 step 3, "decide the envelope
    format," is still from-scratch); (2) there is ZERO signature code anywhere (no verifyMessage/recoverAddress/
    SigningKey) and NO `vh dataset verify-attest` subcommand — so a buyer handed a "signed by the publisher"
    attestation has NO command to confirm the signature is genuine and binds the exact dataset identity. Without
    a verifier, a signature is unfalsifiable decoration.
  - **The insight that makes this auto-buildable WITHOUT touching the guardrail.** The loop must NEVER provision
    or hold a REAL signing key (P-3 step 2, needs-human). But it CAN (a) DEFINE the detached signature envelope
    format — a separate, additive container that WRAPS the canonical unsigned bytes verbatim, never edits them,
    so T-15.2's strict UNSIGNED guarantee is preserved — and (b) BUILD + locally TEST the VERIFIER end-to-end
    using EPHEMERAL, throwaway `Wallet.createRandom()` keys generated in-process (never persisted, never a
    real-funds key). That proves the complete sign→verify loop works and pins down the exact envelope/scheme, so
    P-3 collapses from "design a scheme AND provision a key" to "PROVISION a key and sign with the format we
    already ship + locally proved." ethers 6.17 (already a dependency) provides the recovery primitives — no new
    dependency, no network.
  - **Shape.** T-17.1 defines a versioned, strictly-validated SIGNED-attestation container
    (`verifyhash.dataset-attestation-signed`) that embeds the EXACT canonical unsigned bytes + a
    `{ scheme, signer, signature }` block (`eip191-personal-sign` over those bytes), with the embedded payload
    re-validated by the EXISTING `validateAttestation` (wrap-don't-edit invariant) — pure, no key handling.
    T-17.2 adds `vh dataset verify-attest <signed> [--manifest <m>] [--signer <addr>] [--json]`: an OFFLINE
    verifier that recovers the signer, optionally pins the EXPECTED publisher (`--signer`) and binds the
    signature to the buyer's own dataset (`--manifest` re-derives the canonical bytes), prints ACCEPTED/REJECTED
    with the existing 0/3 CI-exit convention, and is PROVED end-to-end in tests with throwaway keys. T-17.3
    documents it and sharpens the P-3 handoff to provision-only. Every command LEADS with the standing dataset
    TRUST_NOTE plus a signing caveat (a valid signature proves the key-holder vouched for this dataset identity;
    it does NOT by itself prove a trustworthy TIMESTAMP — "unaltered since date T" still needs the human
    trust-root P-3 — and does NOT validate the license/source hints) so it never overclaims past P-3.
  - **Why this beats the alternatives I considered.** (a) Another DataLedger descriptive feature (more summary/
    report/check polish) is the exact capped vein the plateau warns against and would re-cap usefulness at 4.
    (b) EPIC-3 reputation is BLOCKED on D-2 (P-1, human-only) and is a deprioritized crypto feature. (c)
    Standing up a real signing key / TSA is P-3 itself — guardrail-blocked, NOT auto-buildable. Building the
    format + verifier with throwaway keys is the part of P-3's value the loop CAN deliver now, and it directly
    converts P-3 from a design-and-provision task into a provision-only task — sharpening AND de-risking the
    blocker in one EPIC, which is precisely what the value-ceiling directive asks for.
  - **Guardrails respected.** Pure-local, offline, no funds, no deploy, no real key, no token framing — nothing
    here touches D-2/EPIC-4/P-1/P-2 or REVENUE INTEGRITY (no token/coin/NFT/sale/airdrop/staking; income comes
    from selling the product to paying customers, a HUMAN step). No contract change. The UNSIGNED attest path
    and ALL its tests are UNTOUCHED (the signed container WRAPS, never edits) so the gate never regresses. The
    only keys that appear anywhere are ephemeral, in-process `Wallet.createRandom()` test keys, explicitly
    marked test-only and never a real-funds key. No new dependency (ethers already present), no global install,
    no network. P-3 itself stays human-gated; T-17.x ships only the FORMAT + VERIFIER.

- **2026-06-23 — Strategist: open EPIC-16 "DataLedger v1.3: the license-policy gate" — turn DataLedger from
  a tool that DESCRIBES license/source provenance into one that GATES it against a written compliance policy
  (the CI-runnable, auditor-filed control a paying buyer's process is built on).** No pivot; no stack change
  (still Node CLI + Solidity, test command unchanged: `npx hardhat test`).
  - **Stagnation/frontier read (per the directive, acted on).** The build frontier is EMPTY again —
    EPIC-13/14/15 (DataLedger build/verify/prove/diff/summary/report/attest) are all VERIFIED, 743 tests green,
    and the human-gated unlocks (P-1/P-2/P-3) are written. The latest METRICS line (`2026-06-23T19:32:12Z`)
    shows avgUsefulness 4.0 / min 4 with `humanGated: 3` — the persistent flat-and-mediocre plateau the
    directive says to break by pursuing a HIGHER-LEVERAGE capability, not more report/attest/docs polish in the
    same vein. The Critic lens judges revenue-relevance (does each increment move toward a buyer with a
    budgeted, externally-imposed reason to pay: EU-AI-Act technical docs, enterprise data-provenance
    due-diligence). So the correct move is a NEW DataLedger capability that advances the income product toward
    the buyer's actual control.
  - **The gap I found (confirmed against the code, not invented).** I surveyed `cli/dataset.js` (1188 lines),
    `aggregateManifest`, `runDatasetSummary`/`buildDatasetReport`, and grepped for any policy/check/allow/deny/
    compliance verb — there is NONE. DataLedger DESCRIBES license/source provenance (a histogram: "licenses
    seen {MIT:120, GPL-3.0:8, (no license hint):14}") but cannot GATE it. The single most concrete, recurring
    question a compliance reviewer / a CI pipeline asks is not "what licenses are present" — it is "does this
    training set VIOLATE my org's written policy?" (no copyleft in a proprietary product; every file MUST carry
    a license; only an allowlisted set of sources/licenses). Today a human must eyeball the histogram and decide
    PASS/FAIL by hand, every time, with no auditable/repeatable verdict, no CI-gateable exit code, and no
    deterministic list of WHICH files violate WHICH rule. That is the difference between "a provenance report"
    and "a compliance control" — and the control is the artifact a buyer's due-diligence process and CI both
    actually run.
  - **Shape.** T-16.1 adds a small, versioned, strictly-validated POLICY file (allow/deny lists for license and
    source, a `requireLicense` flag — documented exact-match semantics) and `vh dataset check <manifest>
    --policy <p>` — a PURE, deterministic, OFFLINE evaluator over the manifest's TRUSTED per-file {relPath,
    hints} that emits PASS/FAIL + the exact violating files (relPath + rule + value), exit 0/3 mirroring the
    existing `vh dataset verify`/`report` data-divergence convention so all dataset gates share one exit
    contract, `--json` for a pipeline. T-16.2 folds the SAME pure evaluator (verbatim, no re-impl) into `vh
    dataset report --policy` as a "Policy compliance" section so the buyer's filed document shows the verdict,
    with a well-defined combined exit code (`--verify` + `--policy` → exit 3 if EITHER fails) so one report
    invocation is a complete CI gate. T-16.3 documents it. Every command LEADS with the existing dataset
    TRUST_NOTE verbatim — a PASS attests the dataset's UNTRUSTED, self-asserted hints satisfy the policy, NOT
    that the licenses are genuinely correct — so it never overclaims.
  - **Why this beats the alternatives I considered.** (a) EPIC-3 reputation is BLOCKED on D-2 (human-only) and
    is a crypto feature the income pivot deprioritized — not buyer-relevant now. (b) The signing/timestamp
    trust-root (P-3) is the bigger provenance prize but is `needs-human` (real key/TSA custody) — not
    auto-buildable; this EPIC doesn't touch it. (c) More report/attest/docs polish on the existing verbs is the
    exact low-leverage vein the stagnation signal warns against and would re-cap usefulness at 4. A policy GATE
    is a NEW capability that turns DataLedger from a descriptive tool into a CI-gateable compliance control — the
    verb a paying buyer's pipeline and an auditor's checklist actually run — and it is the shared engine the
    sibling products (ProofParcel, AttestKit, which gate delivered data / audit-log evidence against policy)
    reuse on the same core.
  - **Guardrails respected.** Pure-local, offline, no funds, no deploy, no token framing — nothing here touches
    D-2/EPIC-4/P-3 or REVENUE INTEGRITY (no token/coin/NFT/sale/airdrop/staking; income comes from selling the
    product to paying customers, a HUMAN step). No contract change; reuses the existing offline manifest + trusted
    file set + `aggregateManifest`/report core verbatim. The existing dataset/write/read paths and their tests are
    untouched, and the new offline commands need neither a key nor a network, so the test gate never regresses. No
    new dependency, no global install, no network.

- **2026-06-23 — Strategist: open EPIC-15 "DataLedger v1.2: the auditor's filed deliverable" — turn scattered
  CLI output into the ONE document a paying buyer's compliance process consumes, plus the canonical payload the
  human signing trust-root will sign.** No pivot; no stack change (still Node CLI + Solidity, test command
  unchanged: `npx hardhat test`).
