  - **Stagnation/frontier read (per the directive, acted on).** The build frontier is EMPTY — EPIC-13/14
    (DataLedger v1 + v1.1) are all VERIFIED, 701 tests green, and the latest METRICS line shows the multi-run
    plateau with `humanGated: 3` and `newlyPlanned: 0` (nothing left to build). The north star is INCOME from a
    PAYING customer and the Critic lens now judges revenue-relevance (does each increment move toward a buyer
    with a budgeted, externally-imposed reason to pay: EU AI Act technical docs; enterprise data-provenance
    due-diligence). So the correct move is NOT another crypto-core increment in the capped vein — it is to
    advance the income product the LAST mile toward the buyer's actual deliverable.
  - **The gap I found (confirmed against the code, not invented).** Judged through the revenue lens, DataLedger
    emits CORRECT but SCATTERED output: a manifest JSON (`vh dataset build`), a histogram block (`vh dataset
    summary`), and a MATCH/MISMATCH verdict (`vh dataset verify`) — three commands a reviewer must run and
    assemble BY HAND. I surveyed `cli/dataset.js` (1109 lines), `docs/DATALEDGER.md`, and the summary/verify
    result shapes:
    1. *No consolidated evidence report.* The buyer FILES a document (an EU-AI-Act technical-doc section / a
       due-diligence packet), not three terminal outputs. Nothing assembles dataset identity + the
       provenance/license roll-up + an optional live-tree verify status + the trust caveats into one
       deterministic artifact (Markdown to file, `--json` to ingest). The pieces all exist
       (`runDatasetSummary` + `runDatasetVerify` + `TRUST_NOTE`); the assembly — the thing the buyer's process
       is actually built around — does not. T-15.1.
    2. *No canonical, signing-ready attestation payload.* DataLedger's most-repeated limit (it is NOT a
       timestamp) means SIGNING is human-gated (now written as P-3). But the deterministic, canonical BYTES a
       human/timestamp service would sign are fully buildable now, and producing them is the bridge that turns
       the human trust-root step from "design + sign a payload" into "sign THIS exact file." T-15.2 builds that
       UNSIGNED payload (`vh dataset attest`) — explicitly marked unsigned, never overclaiming a timestamp —
       which de-risks and unblocks P-3, the product's biggest provenance unlock.
  - **Shape.** T-15.1 `vh dataset report <manifest> [--verify <dir>] [--json] [--out <p>]` — REUSES
    `runDatasetSummary`'s aggregation + `runDatasetVerify`'s verdict verbatim (no new math), deterministic
    Markdown (stable section + histogram order) / `--json`, optional embedded verify status, exit 0/3 mirroring
    `vh dataset verify` under `--verify`. T-15.2 `vh dataset attest <manifest>` — a versioned, strictly-validated,
    byte-deterministic UNSIGNED envelope (root + fileCount + a canonical `manifestDigest` + caveat), an explicit
    `signed:false` slot, the in-band note pointing at P-3 for the human signing step. T-15.3 documents both in
    docs/DATALEDGER.md + README, reusing the existing TRUST_NOTE so caveats never drift. Each leads with the
    standing dataset trust posture; nothing claims "unaltered since date T".
  - **Why this beats the alternatives I considered.** (a) EPIC-3 reputation is BLOCKED on D-2 (human-only) and is
    a CRYPTO feature the income pivot deprioritized — not buyer-relevant now. (b) The signing/timestamp
    trust-root itself is the bigger prize but is a `needs-human` step (real key/TSA custody) — written as P-3,
    NOT auto-buildable; EPIC-15 builds the deterministic payload it CONSUMES without overclaiming past it. (c)
    More crypto-core CLI/docs polish is the exact low-leverage vein the stagnation signal warns against and would
    re-cap usefulness. The evidence report + canonical attestation payload turn DataLedger from a set of verbs
    into the deliverable a paying buyer's process consumes — the LAST mile toward a design-partner customer — and
    are the foundation the sibling products (ProofParcel, AttestKit) reuse on the same core.
  - **Guardrails respected.** Pure-local, offline, no funds, no deploy, no token framing — nothing here touches
    D-2/EPIC-4 or REVENUE INTEGRITY (no token/coin/NFT/sale/airdrop/staking; income comes from selling the product
    to paying customers, a HUMAN step). No contract change; reuses the existing offline Merkle + summary/verify
    core verbatim. The signing trust-root stays human-gated (P-3); T-15.2 builds only the UNSIGNED payload and
    must not imply otherwise. The existing dataset/write/read paths and their tests are untouched, and the new
    offline commands need neither a key nor a network, so the test gate never regresses. No new dependency, no
    global install, no network.

- **2026-06-23 — OPERATOR DIRECTION (from the human): pivot the north star to INCOME, and EXPAND into a
  product FAMILY on the shared provenance core.** The human asked the loop to "create something useful that
  can generate income" and to "not limit to one thing — keep expanding." A multi-agent ideation study
  (15 ideas generated + scored) chose the direction rather than guessing:
  - **First product: DataLedger — AI training-data provenance & dataset manifests** (top score 24/30). It
    repoints the EXISTING, well-tested core (path-bound Merkle in cli/hash.js, lineage DAG in cli/lineage.js,
    portable offline set-membership proof in cli/proof.js, the receipt-manifest diff in cli/verify.js —
    ~577 passing tests) at a buyer with budgeted, externally-imposed reasons to pay: AI/ML companies facing
    enterprise data-provenance due-diligence and EU AI Act technical documentation. Income = metered
    subscription + on-prem license + paid attested-manifest exports. See EPIC-13.
  - **Crypto was considered and scored LOWER.** The best crypto idea (BuildProof, reproducible-build
    attestation) came 5th — crypto-provenance fights FREE incumbents (Sourcify, SLSA, Sigstore); no payer.
  - **Expansion plan.** DataLedger, ProofParcel (B2B data-delivery receipts), AttestKit (SOC2/ISO audit-log
    evidence) all sit on the SAME core. After DataLedger v1 lands, expand into these as THIN product adapters
    over the shared engine — one core, many paying buyers — rather than scattering effort.
  - **REVENUE INTEGRITY (also encoded in the engine VISION GOAL, gated).** Income MUST come from paying
    customers for real value — NEVER a token/coin/NFT, token sale, airdrop, or staking/yield (a security;
    forbidden by HARD GUARDRAILS). The loop only BUILDS + locally TESTS; landing a design-partner customer,
    a signing/timestamp trust-root, EU-AI-Act field mapping, pricing, billing, and sales are HUMAN steps.
    Building more products multiplies shots on goal; it does NOT by itself produce revenue.

- **2026-06-23 — Strategist: open EPIC-6 "Durable, portable receipts". Make the flagship flows
  operable, not just demonstrable.** No pivot; no stack change (still Node CLI + Solidity, test
  command unchanged: `npx hardhat test`).
  - **Where we are.** EPIC-0 (hardening), EPIC-1 (`hash`/`anchor`/`verify`), EPIC-2 (`prove`) and the
    T-0.3 commit–reveal attribution are all VERIFIED; suite is 113 green. EPIC-3 (reputation) and
    EPIC-4 (deploy) are correctly parked behind human decisions (D-2 token framing, mainnet deploy) and
    must NOT be auto-built. So the frontier of *buildable* value is the gap between "the contract is
    correct" and "a person can actually run these flows end to end without losing data."
  - **Why this next (two concrete holes, both buildable without any human decision).**
    1. *Commit–reveal is not durable.* `runClaim` performs commit AND reveal in one process, holding
       the secret salt only in memory while it waits out `MIN_REVEAL_DELAY`. On a live testnet that wait
       is minutes; a crash/Ctrl-C in between loses the salt forever — the contentHash is then
       committed-but-unrevealable (by anyone, since reveal needs that salt) and the attribution is
       permanently burned. There is no `vh reveal` to resume. For the project's headline
       "front-running-resistant authorship" feature, "you can lose your claim to a process restart" is a
       correctness-grade defect, not a nicety. Fix: persist a versioned claim receipt at commit time and
       add a resumable `vh commit` / `vh reveal` split (T-6.1).
    2. *Directory verify can't localize a tamper.* `vh verify <dir>` only reports root MATCH/MISMATCH;
       for a real repo it can't say which file changed, even though `vh hash` already computes every
       per-file path-bound leaf and then discards them. Fix: record those leaves in the receipt manifest
       and make `vh verify --receipt` print a precise ADDED/REMOVED/CHANGED diff (T-6.2), while the
       authoritative verdict still comes from re-deriving the root vs the on-chain record (the receipt
       stays an untrusted convenience, consistent with TRUST-BOUNDARIES).
  - **Shape.** One small new module `cli/receipt.js` (a versioned JSON schema + strictly-validated
    read/write) carries both: the salt/commitment for resumable claims and the per-file manifest for
    localized diffs. New commands `vh commit` / `vh reveal`; `vh claim` stays as the one-shot
    convenience (and now also drops a receipt). `vh anchor`/`vh verify` gain an optional `--receipt`.
  - **Guardrails respected.** Pure-local, no funds, no deploy, no token framing — nothing here touches
    D-2 or EPIC-4. The legacy single-process `runClaim` path (and its live front-run e2e test) is kept
    working so the test gate never regresses; new behaviour is additive and independently tested.
  - **Explicitly NOT chosen now.** Did not start EPIC-3 reputation (blocked on D-2), did not propose a
    deploy (blocked, human-only), and did not add speculative features (web UI, indexer) before the
    core write/verify loop is actually safe to operate. Durability of the existing flagship feature
    beats new surface area.

- **2026-06-23 — Strategist: open EPIC-7 "Registry read side: discovery + audit". Give the registry a
  read side so it is browsable/auditable, not just appendable.** No pivot; no stack change (still Node
  CLI + Solidity, test command unchanged: `npx hardhat test`).
  - **Where we are.** EPIC-0/1/2 and EPIC-6 (durable, portable receipts) are all VERIFIED; suite is 170
    green. The contract is ownerless, immutable, front-running-resistant (commit–reveal), and the
    write→verify single-item loop (`hash`/`anchor`/`claim`/`commit`/`reveal`/`verify`/`prove`) is
    complete and tested. EPIC-3 (reputation) and EPIC-4 (deploy) remain correctly parked behind human
    decisions (D-2 token framing, mainnet deploy) and must NOT be auto-built.
  - **Why this next (the clearest buildable gap, no human decision needed).** The registry has no READ
    side beyond "tell me about the one hash I already hold the bytes for." The contract already exposes
    `total`, `hashAtIndex(i)`, `getRecord(hash)` and indexed `Anchored`/`Revealed` events, but there is
    NO CLI to enumerate, browse, or audit what has been anchored, and no way for a third party who holds
    only a `contentHash` (from a receipt, a published claim, an event) to look it up on-chain without
    re-deriving it from local content. An immutable public ledger you can only append to and verify
    one-known-item-at-a-time is half a product: discovery, audit, and "look it up by hash" are what make
    it useful to anyone other than the original writer — and they directly feed EPIC-3 later (you cannot
    reward "verified contributions" you cannot enumerate). This is the natural next layer of real value.
  - **Shape.** (1) T-7.1 adds two bounded, paginated, ownerless `view` reads to the contract —
    `getRecordAtIndex(i)` and `getRecords(start, count)` (clamped to `total`, never reverts on an
    out-of-range tail) — so off-chain enumeration is one batched call per page instead of 2·N round-trips,
    while preserving the contract's "no unbounded loop / no gas-DoS" property (the loop is bounded by the
    caller's page size, and these are `eth_call` reads). Purely additive: no new state, no write path,
    same TRUST BOUNDARIES NatSpec. (2) T-7.2 `vh list` enumerates the registry (filters by contributor /
    authorBound, `--limit/--offset`, `--json`), read-only, no key. (3) T-7.3 `vh show <0xhash>` looks up
    a single record by hash with no local content, distinguishing NotAnchored from a real RPC error
    exactly as `verify.js` already does. (4) T-7.4 documents the read side and cross-links it.
  - **Guardrails respected.** Pure-local, no funds, no deploy, no token framing — nothing here touches
    D-2 or EPIC-4. New contract code is read-only/additive and goes through the same test gate; the read
    commands need only an RPC URL. The existing write/verify paths and their tests are untouched, so the
    gate never regresses.
  - **Explicitly NOT chosen now.** Did not start EPIC-3 reputation (blocked on D-2), did not propose a
    deploy (human-only), and did not jump to a web UI / hosted indexer before the CLI even has a read
    command — the local, dependency-free read side comes first and is what any future indexer/UI would
    build on. Making the registry browsable beats adding more write-side surface area.

- **2026-06-23 — Strategist: open EPIC-8 "Git-scoped, reproducible anchoring". Make the tool actually fit
  its stated purpose — a registry of CODE CONTRIBUTIONS, not arbitrary filesystem trees.** No pivot; no
  stack change (still Node CLI + Solidity, test command unchanged: `npx hardhat test`).
  - **Where we are.** EPIC-0/1/2/6/7 are all VERIFIED; suite is 250 green. The write→verify→read loop
    (`hash`/`anchor`/`claim`/`commit`/`reveal`/`verify`/`prove`/`list`/`show`) is complete, the contract
    is ownerless/immutable/front-running-resistant, and receipts make claims durable + directory tampers
    localizable. EPIC-3 (reputation) and EPIC-4 (deploy) remain correctly parked behind human decisions
    (D-2 token framing, mainnet deploy) and must NOT be auto-built.
  - **Why this next (a foundational mismatch, fully buildable, no human decision).** I surveyed cli/
    and found that for a project whose headline is "registry of code contributions," `vh hash <dir>`
    (cli/hash.js › `listFiles`) walks the RAW filesystem with no exclusions — it hashes `.git/`,
    `node_modules/`, build artifacts, `.env`, and editor junk indiscriminately. Three correctness/value
    consequences, all confirmed against the code:
    1. *Not reproducible across clones.* Two people anchoring "the same commit" get DIFFERENT roots
       because of untracked files, local build output, `.git` internals, and OS/line-ending/permission
       drift. A verifier who clones the repo cannot re-derive the anchored root — which directly
       contradicts the README's core promise ("anyone can later prove some content is byte-for-byte what
       was anchored — without trusting any server"). The single-file path is fine; the DIRECTORY path,
       which is what a "repo contribution" actually is, is not reproducible.
    2. *No git-commit binding.* The natural unit of a code contribution is a git tree/commit, yet there
       is no way to anchor "repo at commit abc123" reproducibly — you can only hash whatever is on disk.
    3. *Anchoring secrets/junk.* Silently hashing `.env`/secrets/`node_modules` is a privacy footgun and
       the chief source of the non-determinism above.
  - **Shape.** A new `cli/git.js` (pure helpers over `git`, invoked with argv arrays + `cwd`, never a
    shell string — NUL-delimited `ls-tree -r -z` for path safety) enumerates exactly the files git tracks
    at a chosen ref. `vh hash/anchor/verify --git [--ref]` feed THAT file set through the EXISTING
    path-bound, sorted-leaf Merkle machinery unchanged — same `DIR_LEAF_DOMAIN`/`LEAF_TAG`/`NODE_TAG`,
    same on-chain `verifyLeaf`, no contract change and no new leaf scheme (only the file SET differs, so
    docs/MERKLE-LEAVES.md still applies). The git provenance (commit oid + scope) rides along in the
    receipt as an UNTRUSTED hint (T-8.2), and verify re-derives the tracked set so a clone of the same
    commit reproduces the root and reports MATCH end-to-end. T-8.3 documents it. Non-`--git` behaviour is
    byte-for-byte unchanged so no existing test regresses.
  - **Why this beats the alternatives I considered.** (a) EPIC-3 reputation is the bigger prize but is
    blocked on D-2 (token framing, human-only) — cannot auto-build. (b) A web UI / hosted indexer is
    premature: it would index a registry whose CORE artifact (a repo root) isn't yet reproducible, so it
    would bake the defect in. (c) More read-side polish has diminishing returns — the read side is
    complete. Making a "code contribution" actually mean a reproducible, git-pinned thing is the missing
    foundation that EVERY later layer (reputation keyed to "verified contributions," any indexer, any
    deploy story) depends on. Fixing reproducibility before adding surface area is the right order.
  - **Guardrails respected.** Pure-local, no funds, no deploy, no token framing — nothing here touches
    D-2 or EPIC-4. `git` is already on PATH (2.34.1); no new dependency, no global install, no network.
    Helpers shell out with argv arrays (no shell-injection surface) and read-only over the work tree. The
    existing write/verify/read paths and their tests are untouched, so the test gate never regresses.

- **2026-06-23 — Strategist: open EPIC-9 "Don't scatter secrets; make proofs portable". Close a real
  security/operability footgun and complete the project's headline promise.** No pivot; no stack change
  (still Node CLI + Solidity, test command unchanged: `npx hardhat test`).
  - **Where we are.** EPIC-0/1/2/6/7/8 are all VERIFIED; suite is 309 green. The
    write→verify→read→git-scoped loop is complete, the contract is ownerless/immutable/front-running-
    resistant, receipts make claims durable + tampers localizable, and `--git` makes a repo root
    reproducible. EPIC-3 (reputation) and EPIC-4 (deploy) remain correctly parked behind human decisions
    (D-2 token framing, mainnet deploy) and must NOT be auto-built.
  - **Why this next (two concrete, fully-buildable gaps; no human decision).**
    1. *We silently drop SECRET-bearing files into the operator's working tree.* `runClaim`/`runCommit`
       default the receipt path to `defaultReceiptPath(contentHash)` → `./<prefix>.vhclaim.json` resolved
       against `process.cwd()` (cli/receipt.js:514). A user who runs `vh claim`/`vh commit` from inside
       their own repo gets a file holding a **plaintext secret `salt`** dropped into their repo root —
       trivially `git add -A`-able and committable (it is only gitignored in THIS project). The same defect
       leaks into our suite: `test/cli.claim.test.js:227` calls `runClaim` from `cwd`=repo-root with no
       explicit path, dropping a fresh secret-bearing `*.vhclaim.json` into the repo root **every run**
       (4 present now; growing — the Manager has flagged this 3× but no builder had a mandate to FIX it,
       only a reviewer to RE-FLAG it). A registry tool whose flagship attribution flow scatters secret
       material into the user's working directory is a correctness/security defect, not cosmetics. T-9.1
       makes the in-process helper require an explicit path (no silent cwd write), makes `vh commit` name
       the exact file it wrote, isolates every test's receipt to an OS temp dir, asserts the suite leaves
       ZERO receipts in the repo root, and deletes the stale leaks.
    2. *Proofs can't leave the prover's machine.* `vh prove` (cli/prove.js) builds a genuine Merkle proof
       but only PRINTS it or checks it on-chain in-process — there is no shareable artifact and no consumer
       command. So a third party handed "file X is in anchored repo root R" cannot independently verify it
       without re-running the prover against the prover's own working tree. That directly contradicts the
       README's core promise ("anyone can later prove some content is byte-for-byte what was anchored —
       without trusting any server"). T-9.2 adds `vh prove --out <p>` (a versioned, self-contained proof
       artifact) and a new read-only `vh verify-proof <p>` that re-folds the proof OFFLINE and confirms the
       root is anchored on-chain — needing only the artifact + an RPC URL, no repo, no key. T-9.3 documents
       both.
  - **Shape.** T-9.1 is a focused safety fix across cli/claim.js + tests (+ doc note). T-9.2 adds a small
    proof-artifact module reusing receipt.js's strict-validation style and hash.js's EXISTING
    `leafHash`/`nodeHash`/leaf construction and the contract's `verifyLeaf` (no new Merkle scheme, no
    contract change). T-9.3 is pure docs. New behaviour is additive; non-`--out`/`prove` paths and their
    tests are untouched so the gate never regresses.
  - **Why this beats the alternatives I considered.** (a) EPIC-3 reputation is the bigger prize but is
    blocked on D-2 (human-only) — cannot auto-build. (b) A web UI / hosted indexer is premature and would
    sit atop a tool that still leaks secrets and can't export a proof. (c) More read-side/CLI polish has
    diminishing returns. Fixing a secret-leaking footgun is the highest-priority *correctness* work
    available, and making proofs portable is the missing half of the project's stated reason to exist —
    both are foundations every later layer (reputation keyed to *verifiable* contributions, any indexer,
    any deploy story) depends on. Safety + completing the headline promise beats new surface area.
  - **Guardrails respected.** Pure-local, no funds, no deploy, no token framing — nothing touches D-2 or
    EPIC-4. No new dependency, no global install, no network. The existing write/verify/read/git paths and
    their tests are untouched; the new verify-proof path needs only an RPC URL (no key). Tests self-clean
    to a temp dir so the gate stays green AND the working tree stays clean.

- **2026-06-23 — Strategist: open EPIC-10 "Contribution lineage". Give the registry a verifiable,
  tamper-evident contribution GRAPH — the higher-leverage move the quality-stagnation signal calls for.**
  No pivot; no stack change (still Node CLI + Solidity, test command unchanged: `npx hardhat test`).
  - **Stagnation read (per the directive).** Last METRICS lines show tasks keep VERIFYING but usefulness
    has plateaued: avg 4.5 / min 4, and the Manager's own analysis confirms the only sub-5 scores are
    pure-documentation tasks (an inherently capped category) while the read side is "complete" and "more
    polish has diminishing returns." That is exactly the correct-but-low-leverage pattern the directive
    says to break by changing approach MATERIALLY — pursuing a capability that unlocks NEW value, not more
    incremental items in the same `hash/anchor/verify/list/show/prove + docs` vein. So I did not plan
    another CLI-polish or docs task; I went looking for a missing primitive.
  - **The gap I found (confirmed against the code).** The contract's `Record` is a FLAT ISLAND
    (contributor, authorBound, timestamp, blockNumber, uri). I grepped the entire contract, cli/, and
    test/ for any notion of parent/predecessor/revision/lineage/supersede — there is NONE. Yet the
    project's whole stated trajectory is "registry of code CONTRIBUTIONS → decentralized contribution
    org," and a contribution is inherently a thing that EVOLVES: v2 fixes v1, a fork derives from an
    upstream, a patch builds on a base. The registry currently cannot express the single most basic
    relationship a contribution has — "this came after / revises / builds on that." It is a pile of
    unrelated hashes, not a contribution history.
  - **Shape.** A new on-chain primitive: a record may optionally reference ONE already-anchored
    predecessor contentHash (a `bytes32 parent`, 0x0 == lineage root). Because a parent MUST pre-exist
    before it can be named, the structure is a DAG BY CONSTRUCTION — acyclic, O(1) per write (one mapping
    existence check, NO loop / no chain-walk on-chain), so the contract's hard invariants are all preserved
    (ownerless, immutable, first-writer-wins, no unbounded loop / no gas-DoS, non-payable). T-10.1 adds
    `anchorWithParent`/`revealWithParent` (legacy `anchor`/`reveal` unchanged, delegating with parent=0x0),
    a `UnknownParent`/`SelfParent` revert pair, the `parent` field on the returned struct, and a
    log shape (`Linked` or extended events) an indexer reconstructs the graph from. T-10.2 wires it into
    the CLI: `vh anchor/claim --parent <hash>` (write a revision) and a new read-only `vh lineage <hash>`
    that walks the parent chain up to the root (bounded by `--max-depth`, no key, `--json`), plus a
    `parent` line on `vh show`. T-10.3 documents the graph in a new `docs/LINEAGE.md` and cross-links it.
  - **Why this is the right leverage and not scope-creep.** This is the SUBSTRATE EPIC-3 (reputation keyed
    to verified contributions) will later flow along — reputation for a v3 that builds on v1/v2 needs an
    edge to flow over — but it is NOT itself reputation/token work, so it touches D-2 not at all and needs
    NO human decision and NO deploy. It is a pure structural extension of the immutable on-chain data +
    read/verify side, built with the exact same discipline (full TRUST-BOUNDARIES NatSpec: a parent edge is
    the CHILD author's CLAIM of a predecessor — it does not prove genuine ancestry, consumers re-derive
    both, and it does not transfer authorship). It makes the registry a graph you can WALK and AUDIT
    ("show the full revision history of this contribution and who authored each step"), which is new,
    auditable value rather than polish.
  - **Why this beats the alternatives I considered.** (a) EPIC-3 reputation is the bigger prize but is
    BLOCKED on D-2 (token framing, human-only) — cannot auto-build, and is premature without a lineage
    substrate to key reputation to. (b) A web UI / hosted indexer is premature surface area atop a registry
    that can't yet express the most basic contribution relationship; it would index a flat list. (c) More
    CLI/doc polish is the exact low-leverage vein the stagnation signal warns against. Lineage is a NEW
    capability, unblocked, and the natural foundation every later layer (reputation, indexer, deploy story)
    will build on. Fixing the missing graph primitive before adding more surface area is the right order.
  - **Guardrails respected.** Pure-local, no funds, no deploy, no token framing — nothing here touches D-2
    or EPIC-4. New contract code is additive and goes through the same test gate; the legacy `anchor`/
    `reveal` paths and ALL existing tests are untouched so the gate never regresses; the new read command
    needs only an RPC URL (no key). No new dependency, no global install, no network.

- **2026-06-23 — Strategist: complete EPIC-10 by closing the in-code FOLLOW-UP (B-10.1) — thread the
  lineage `--parent` edge through the RESUMABLE commit/reveal receipt — rather than adding another docs
  task.** No pivot; no stack change (still Node CLI + Solidity, test command unchanged: `npx hardhat test`).
  - **Stagnation read (per the directive).** The last METRICS line (`2026-06-23T09:46:00Z`) shows
    avgUsefulness 4.5 / minUsefulness 4 — a flat-and-mediocre plateau. The Manager's own analysis (Team
    changes log) confirms the only sub-5 scores are pure-documentation tasks (an inherently capped category)
    while substantive tasks score 5/5. The directive says to break this by pursuing a CAPABILITY that unlocks
    value, not more incremental docs/CLI polish in the same vein. So I did NOT plan another docs task; I went
    looking for an unbuilt capability.
  - **The gap I found (confirmed against the code, not invented).** EPIC-10 is marked all-VERIFIED, but it
    left an EXPLICIT, in-code FOLLOW-UP unbuilt — labelled "B-10.1" in BACKLOG (T-10.1/T-10.2 prose) and
    enforced by a live hard-error at `cli/vh.js:604-610`. The resumable, crash-durable claim path
    (`vh commit` persists a receipt → later `vh reveal --receipt` resumes from a fresh process) CANNOT carry
    a `--parent` lineage edge: the claim-receipt schema (`cli/receipt.js`, SCHEMA_VERSION 3) has no `parent`
    field; `buildCommitTx`/`runCommit` neither accept nor persist a parent; `runReveal` calls the LEGACY
    no-parent `contract.reveal(...)` even though the contract ALREADY ships `revealWithParent`; and
    `vh commit --parent` HARD-ERRORS. So the ONLY way to record a commit-reveal lineage edge today is the
    one-shot `vh claim --parent` — which is exactly the non-durable path EPIC-6 existed to replace (salt held
    in memory across MIN_REVEAL_DELAY, lost on a crash). Net: a contributor cannot simultaneously have (a)
    front-running-resistant authorship, (b) a recorded lineage edge, and (c) crash-durability. That trifecta
    is the whole point of the flagship flow — this is a real operability hole, not polish.
  - **Shape.** A versioned receipt schema bump v3→v4 (additive OPTIONAL `parent` on the claim receipt,
    mirroring exactly how `git`/`manifest` were added — `_attachOptional` + a `_normParent` normalizer; older
    receipts still read), then thread `parent` through `buildCommitTx`→`runCommit` (persist it, validated up
    front via the EXISTING `normalizeParent` before any network call) and `runReveal` (route to the existing
    `buildRevealTx`/`revealWithParent` when the receipt carries a parent). Remove the `vh commit --parent`
    hard-error. The commit() tx is unchanged — the edge is recorded at REVEAL time, so the commitment binding
    is byte-identical with or without a parent — which also gives a clean, documented failure mode: a
    stale/unanchored parent fails the REVEAL (`UnknownParent`), not the commit, leaving the receipt reusable.
    B-10.2 documents it. Non-`--parent` commit/reveal behaviour is byte-for-byte unchanged so no existing test
    regresses.
  - **Why this beats the alternatives I considered.** (a) EPIC-3 reputation is the bigger prize but is BLOCKED
    on D-2 (token framing, human-only) — cannot auto-build, and is premature without the lineage substrate
    finished. (b) Another docs/CLI-polish task is the exact low-leverage vein the stagnation signal warns
    against, and would re-cap usefulness at 4. (c) A web UI / hosted indexer is premature surface area atop a
    flagship flow that still can't durably record a lineage edge. Finishing the lineage capability EPIC-10
    started — so the registry's headline flow actually delivers authorship-safety + lineage + durability
    together — is the highest-leverage UNBLOCKED move, and it is a capability completion, not polish.
  - **Guardrails respected.** Pure-local, no funds, no deploy, no token framing — nothing here touches D-2 or
    EPIC-4. The contract is UNCHANGED (it already has `revealWithParent`); this is a CLI + receipt-schema
    thread-through only. The legacy no-parent commit/reveal paths and ALL existing tests are untouched, and
    new receipt-writing tests isolate to an OS temp dir so the hygiene guard (zero `*.vhclaim.json` in the
    repo root) and the test gate both stay green. No new dependency, no global install, no network.

- **2026-06-23 — Strategist: open EPIC-11 "Don't trust the server you read from". Make the read side
  AUTHENTICATE the registry before believing it — closing the last hole in the project's headline
  promise.** No pivot; no stack change (still Node CLI + Solidity, test command unchanged: `npx hardhat test`).
  - **Stagnation read (per the directive).** The last METRICS line (`2026-06-23T09:46:00Z`) shows
    avgUsefulness 4.5 / minUsefulness 4 — a flat-and-mediocre plateau. The Manager's analysis confirms the
    only sub-5 scores are pure-documentation tasks (an inherently capped category) while substantive tasks
    score 5/5, and that the read side is "complete" with "more polish [having] diminishing returns." That
    is exactly the correct-but-low-leverage pattern the directive says to break by changing approach
    MATERIALLY — a capability that unlocks NEW value, not more incremental items in the same
    `hash/anchor/verify/list/show/lineage + docs` vein. So I did NOT plan another CLI/docs task; I went
    looking for a foundational gap.
  - **The contradiction I found (confirmed against the code, not invented).** The project's entire reason
    to exist (README, first paragraph) is "anyone can later prove some content is byte-for-byte what was
    anchored — WITHOUT TRUSTING ANY SERVER." But every read command — `vh verify` (cli/verify.js:241),
    `vh show` (cli/show.js:241), `vh list`, `vh lineage`, and crucially `vh verify-proof` (cli/proof.js) —
    does `new Contract(address, ABI, provider)` and BLINDLY BELIEVES whatever comes back. I grepped the
    whole read path: ZERO `getCode`/bytecode checks, ZERO contract-identity checks, ZERO chainId
    cross-checks. Two concrete, currently-silent failures follow:
    1. *A rogue/wrong contract fabricates verdicts.* The `(rpc, address)` pair a consumer uses itself comes
       from an UNTRUSTED source — the prover, a receipt's `contractAddress` field, a README, a forwarded
       `Anchored` event. A malicious contract that implements the same ABI shape and returns
       `isAnchored=true` / fake records makes the CLI print MATCH / ACCEPTED. The consumer is silently
       trusting exactly the server the promise says they should not have to. The contract carries NO
       on-chain identity marker (no `REGISTRY_ID`/`version`/ERC-165 — confirmed), so off-chain code
       currently CANNOT distinguish the real registry from a look-alike even if it tried.
    2. *A receipt/artifact's claimed network is never enforced.* A proof artifact (T-9.2) and a claim
       receipt already record the `chainId` they were anchored on, but `vh verify-proof` never checks that
       the provider it is handed is actually on that chain. So an artifact that says "anchored on chainId
       137" can be "verified" against an attacker's local chain that returns fakes — a false ACCEPTED.
  - **Shape.** T-11.1 gives the contract a cheap, immutable, ownerless IDENTITY marker
    (`REGISTRY_ID = keccak256("verifyhash.ContributionRegistry.v1")` + `REGISTRY_VERSION`, optionally an
    ERC-165 `supportsInterface`) — purely additive, no storage/event/error/struct change, no new write
    surface, so every existing contract test passes byte-for-byte. T-11.2 adds a shared, reusable
    `cli/registry.js › assertRegistry({ provider, contractAddress, expectedChainId? })` preflight wired
    into EVERY read command BEFORE any record is read: (a) `getCode` proves a contract is actually there;
    (b) `REGISTRY_ID()`/`REGISTRY_VERSION()` prove it is genuinely a verifyhash registry, not a lying
    look-alike; (c) when a receipt/artifact supplies an `expectedChainId`, it is cross-checked against
    `provider.getNetwork().chainId` so a verdict is never reported against the wrong network. A genuine
    RPC error is re-thrown as itself (never masqueraded as an identity failure, mirroring the existing
    `isNotAnchoredError` discipline). The human output gains a "registry authenticated" line and `--json`
    a `registry` block; a LOUD, non-default `--skip-identity-check` opt-out exists only for a known
    local-dev contract. T-11.3 documents it. New behaviour is additive; the write path
    (anchor/claim/commit/reveal) is untouched; the live-hardhat-node tests pass the identity check WITHOUT
    the opt-out because the deployed test contract IS a real registry after T-11.1.
  - **Why this beats the alternatives I considered.** (a) EPIC-3 reputation is the bigger prize but is
    BLOCKED on D-2 (token framing, human-only) — cannot auto-build, AND reputation keyed to records read
    from a spoofable registry would inherit this exact hole. (b) A web UI / hosted indexer is premature
    surface area and would BAKE IN the defect: an indexer that trusts whatever RPC it is configured with
    IS the very "trusted server" the project promises to remove. (c) More CLI/docs polish is the exact
    low-leverage vein the stagnation signal warns against and would re-cap usefulness at 4. Authenticating
    the registry before believing it is a NEW capability (a trust-establishment layer), the highest-leverage
    UNBLOCKED move, and the prerequisite that makes the read side — and EVERYTHING built on it — actually
    deliver the headline promise.
  - **Guardrails respected.** Pure-local, no funds, no deploy, no token framing — nothing here touches D-2
    or EPIC-4. New contract code is additive/immutable/ownerless and goes through the same test gate; the
    legacy paths and ALL existing tests are untouched so the gate never regresses; the new preflight needs
    only an RPC URL (no key). No new dependency, no global install, no network.

- **2026-06-23 — Strategist: BREAK THE PLATEAU two ways — (1) finally write the human-gated blocker as a
  decision-ready proposal, and (2) open EPIC-12 "Contribution reputation: the D-2-INDEPENDENT substrate" —
  a genuinely NEW capability (per-contributor verifiable contribution scoring) that needs NO token
  decision.** No pivot; no stack change (still Node CLI + Solidity, test command unchanged: `npx hardhat
  test`).
  - **Stagnation read (per the directive, acted on — not just recited).** The last METRICS lines show a
    hard, multi-run plateau: `avgUsefulness` 4.5 → 4.0, `minUsefulness` stuck at 4, tasks all VERIFYING.
    The Manager's 2026-06-23 analysis is decisive and I am treating it as the controlling signal: even
    SUBSTANTIVE contract/CLI work (T-11.1 frozen identity marker, B-10.1 lineage thread-through) now caps
    at 4/5, and the root cause is structural — the project's real value unlock (EPIC-3 reputation) is
    BLOCKED on D-2 (token framing), cited 15+ times but NEVER written as an actionable human proposal, so
    the loop keeps shipping correct-but-capped scaffolding (EPIC-6→11) around an already-complete core. The
    Critic lens was just modified to flag exactly this. Continuing to add an EPIC-12-of-more-hardening in
    the same vein is the precise low-leverage trap the directive warns against. So this run does the two
    materially-different things the signal demands.
  - **(1) Surface the blocker (the never-done, highest-leverage item).** Wrote `P-1` (D-2 token framing)
    and `P-2` (deployment / EPIC-4) into the `needs-human` section as sharp options/tradeoffs/
    recommended-default proposals a human can actually act on. P-1's recommended default is Option A
    (non-transferable, soulbound reputation-only) — essentially zero securities exposure, fits the stated
    "contribution ORG" goal, and is exactly the cap EPIC-12's substrate is designed for. This turns a
    15×-cited dead end into a decision, which is the only path to >4/5 value the Manager identified.
  - **(2) Build what does NOT need the decision (the new capability).** The KEY insight that unblocks
    auto-buildable reputation work: a "contribution score" is a PURE, DERIVED, NON-TRANSFERABLE VIEW over
    records that ALREADY exist — it is not a token, not transferable, not a security. D-2 is ONLY about
    whether to layer a *transferable/tradeable* token on top (Option B). So the entire reputation
    SUBSTRATE — per-contributor aggregation + a `vh reputation <addr>` read that scores verified
    contributions, weighting `authorBound` (proven first claimant) over front-runnable plain anchors — is
    fully buildable today with NO D-2 decision, NO funds, NO deploy. I confirmed against the contract that
    there is currently NO per-contributor aggregation: `_records` is keyed by contentHash and
    `_hashByIndex` by insertion order; computing "how many verified contributions does address X have"
    costs an off-chain page-walk of all N records. EPIC-12 adds a bounded, additive, ownerless on-chain
    per-contributor index (so scoring is O(contributor's own records), not O(N)) and a read-only
    `vh reputation` command. This is the substrate EPIC-3 (Option A) becomes a thin additive layer over —
    it makes the registry answer "who are the real contributors and how much have they verifiably
    contributed," the exact question the "decentralized contribution org" trajectory depends on.
  - **Shape.** T-12.1: additive ownerless on-chain reads — a per-contributor count + a paginated
    `getRecordsByContributor(addr, start, count)` (same clamped/forgiving pagination + bounded-loop
    discipline as `getRecords`, no new write surface, no storage change to the write path beyond an
    append-only index updated O(1) in the shared `_record` writer, full TRUST-BOUNDARIES NatSpec). T-12.2:
    `vh reputation <addr>` read-only command (authenticated via the EPIC-11 `assertRegistry` preflight, no
    key) that reports a contributor's verified-contribution score — total records, authorBound vs
    anchor-only breakdown, lineage-root vs revision counts — leading with the trust caveat that a score is
    DERIVED from on-chain records and is only as meaningful as the authorBound bar (a plain `anchor` is
    front-runnable, so anchor-only count is explicitly weaker). T-12.3 documents the score's exact
    definition + what it does and does NOT prove (anti-sybil notes; it is NOT a token).
  - **Why this beats the alternatives I considered.** (a) Another EPIC of read/CLI/docs polish on the
    single-item loop is the exact capped vein. (b) A web UI / hosted indexer is premature surface area and
    would index a registry that still can't even answer "who contributed how much." (c) Jumping straight
    into EPIC-3's token contract is blocked on D-2 — which is why this run instead WRITES the D-2 proposal
    AND builds the part of reputation that D-2 does not gate. The substrate is the highest-leverage
    UNBLOCKED move and the natural foundation EPIC-3 (whichever D-2 option the human picks) builds on.
  - **Guardrails respected.** Pure-local, no funds, no deploy, no token framing — the on-chain reads are
    additive/immutable/ownerless and the score is a non-transferable DERIVED view, so nothing here is a
    token, a security, or fund custody (D-2/EPIC-4 stay human-gated as P-1/P-2). The legacy write/read
    paths and ALL existing tests are untouched so the gate never regresses; the new command needs only an
    RPC URL (no key). No new dependency, no global install, no network.

- **2026-06-23 — Strategist: open EPIC-14 "DataLedger v1.1: the auditor's deliverables" — turn the verifiable
  manifest into the artifacts a PAYING buyer actually consumes.** No pivot; no stack change (still Node CLI +
  Solidity, test command unchanged: `npx hardhat test`).
  - **Stagnation read (per the directive, acted on).** The last METRICS lines show the multi-run plateau persists
    and just hit a new low through the pivot — avgUsefulness 4.5 → 4.0 → 3.75 → 4.25, min stuck at 3–4, with
    `humanGated: 3` and the latest run `newlyPlanned: 0` (the build frontier is EMPTY). The Manager's analysis is
    decisive: the project PIVOTED its north star to INCOME this run and shipped EPIC-13 DataLedger v1
    (`vh dataset build/verify/prove/verify-proof`, 658 tests green), and the Critic lens was retargeted to judge
    whether each increment moves toward a PAYING customer (EU AI Act technical docs; enterprise data-provenance
    due-diligence). So the correct move is NOT another crypto-core increment in the capped vein — it is to advance
    the income product toward the buyer.
  - **The gap I found (confirmed against the code, not invented).** Judged through the retargeted Critic lens,
    DataLedger v1 produces a verifiable per-file manifest but NOT the two artifacts the buyer's process actually
    centers on, and it is undocumented as a product. I surveyed `cli/dataset.js`, `cli/receipt.js` (`diffManifest`),
    `README.md`, and `docs/`:
    1. *No dataset-version diff.* The single most common auditor / EU-AI-Act question is "what CHANGED in the
       training data between model version N and N+1?" The only diff today (`vh dataset verify <dir> --manifest`)
       needs the live tree on disk and answers "did THIS tree drift from its OWN manifest." There is NO
       manifest-to-manifest compare — yet both manifests already carry every {relPath, contentHash, leaf}, so the
       comparison is PURELY OFFLINE (no datasets, no key, no network) and reuses `diffManifest` verbatim.
    2. *No provenance/license summary.* v1 records per-file {source, license} as untrusted hints but offers NO
       aggregate roll-up — yet "this dataset is N files; licenses seen {MIT:120, CC-BY:30, UNKNOWN:14}; files with
       no license hint: 14" IS the deliverable a due-diligence reviewer reads. Pure aggregation, no crypto, no network.
    3. *DataLedger is undocumented as a product.* README has a section for every crypto feature but NONE for
       `vh dataset`; there is no `docs/DATALEDGER.md`. A product meant to be evaluated and SOLD needs a buyer-facing
       doc (what it proves, what it does NOT prove — the timestamp/signing trust-root stays human-gated, don't
       overclaim "unaltered since date T" — the build→diff→summary→prove workflow, and the EU-AI-Act/due-diligence
       evidence mapping).
  - **Shape.** T-14.1 `vh dataset diff <manifestA> <manifestB>` (offline, reuses `diffManifest`; exit 3 on differ /
    0 on identical so CI can gate "training set changed unexpectedly"; `--json`). T-14.2 `vh dataset summary
    <manifest>` (offline license/source histogram over the trusted file set, no-hint files in an explicit bucket,
    trust caveat leading). T-14.3 the buyer-facing `docs/DATALEDGER.md` + a README `### Dataset provenance` section.
    Each leads with the existing dataset TRUST_NOTE so the untrusted-hint / no-timestamp caveats never drift.
  - **Why this beats the alternatives I considered.** (a) EPIC-3 reputation is BLOCKED on D-2 (human-only) and is a
    CRYPTO feature the income pivot deprioritized — not buyer-relevant now. (b) The human-owned signing/timestamp
    trust-root is the bigger provenance prize but is a needs-human step (real trust anchor / key custody) — it stays
    in STRATEGY.md, not auto-buildable, and EPIC-14 deliberately does NOT overclaim past it. (c) More crypto-side
    CLI/docs polish is the exact low-leverage vein the stagnation signal warns against and would re-cap usefulness.
    The manifest diff + provenance summary are NEW capabilities that turn a verifiable file list into the
    deliverables a paying buyer's process is built around, and they are the foundation the sibling products
    (ProofParcel, AttestKit) reuse on the same core.
  - **Guardrails respected.** Pure-local, offline, no funds, no deploy, no token framing — nothing here touches
    D-2/EPIC-4 or REVENUE INTEGRITY (no token/coin/NFT/sale/airdrop/staking; income comes from selling the product
    to paying customers, a HUMAN step). No contract change; reuses the existing offline Merkle + `diffManifest` core.
    The existing dataset/write/read paths and their tests are untouched, and the new offline commands need neither a
    key nor a network, so the test gate never regresses. No new dependency, no global install, no network.

## Loop upgrades (archived)

- **2026-07-06 — PROMOTED (engine #32, Architect-authored): run-shape telemetry (`rounds` + `spentTokens`) in the METRICS line.**
  The driver now serializes two additional fields into the per-run METRICS `stats` line — `"rounds":${rounds}` and
  `"spentTokens":${budget.spent()}` (the latter captured at Report-phase entry, excluding only the reporter/architect/
  gatekeeper tail-spend). Motivation: this run's `endReason` hit `"run-cap"` for the FIRST time with verified=1 (vs
  4-6 verified in each of the five prior runs), and the recorded line could NOT distinguish the cause — plan/decide/
  strategize ROUND-CHURN (rounds high, iter=1) vs one enormously expensive build/verify/panel cycle (rounds≈iter) vs a
  launcher-lowered runCapTokens — because `rounds` and `budget.spent()` were logged transiently but never persisted.
  Same additive precedent as endReason/blockedReasons/panelSize/reworkLifted; compounds after 2026-07-08 when Fable
  leaves and first shots fall back to Opus (per-run token magnitude becomes the binding constraint). Diff is a single
  stats-line edit + one explanatory comment; `rounds` and `budget.spent()` are both in scope (the smoke harness ran the
  full engine body to a returned result with no ReferenceError), and no gate, cap, schema, control-flow, driver-script,
  or guardrail (NEVER push/deploy) change — both METRICS consumers (reconcile-run / pre-run-gate) parse lines field-
  agnostically. Gates: `validate-driver.cjs` → PASS and `smoke-driver.cjs` → SMOKE-PASS (5 scenarios: verify-before-
  commit + gatekeeper-invocation + FAILING-verdict / testsPass:false / mechanical runner-red all BLOCK-with-no-commit).
  md5 `3e87857732dd900c49d9e6685de52eaa`; prior engine (#31) backed up to `build-loop.prev.js`.

- **2026-07-05 — PROMOTED (engine #30, Architect-authored): ground-truth task ledger for the Reporter.**
  The driver now serializes its authoritative per-task record (`results[]` — id, title, status, usefulness,
  attempts, reverted-rework, block reason) into a `taskLedger` string and passes it to `reporterPrompt`, which
  pins the MORNING.md "what got built / what's blocked" narrative to EXACTLY those tasks (no fabrication, no
  carry-over from a stale MORNING.md). Fixes the run wf_19281ba9 defect where the haiku Reporter invented
  EPIC-73 funnel work that never ran and the supervisor had to hand-correct the file — the same recall-vs-
  transcription fix the METRICS half of the prompt already used. Diff is purely additive (one derived string +
  one prompt param + a comment); `results` is in scope (declared line 470); no gate, cap, schema, control-flow,
  driver-script, or guardrail (NEVER push/deploy) change. Gates: `validate-driver.cjs` → PASS and
  `smoke-driver.cjs` → SMOKE-PASS (5 scenarios, incl. verify-before-commit + gatekeeper-invocation + BLOCK-no-
  commit paths). md5 `24eba6647d7698b3c710ba0672ae7221`; prior engine backed up to `build-loop.prev.js`.

- **2026-07-06 — PROMOTED (engine #31, Architect-authored): rework-lift telemetry.** The driver now declares a
  `reworkLifted` counter, snapshots the pre-rework panel median as `preReworkUsefulness` just before the
  dissenter-only re-score, increments `reworkLifted` when the post-rework score comes back strictly higher, and
  emits it in the METRICS stats line (`"reworkLifted":…`). This makes the usefulness-floor (<=3) + harsh-dissent
  rework trigger's payoff a DIRECT read across runs — lifted vs reverted (`reworkReverted`) vs flat
  (`rework − reworkReverted − reworkLifted`) — instead of an inference from the task-mix-confounded avgUsefulness
  trend; it matters more after 2026-07-08, when every rework builder/verifier falls back to Opus exactly as budget
  tightens (if lift stays ~0 a future Architect narrows/drops the floor trigger on evidence). Diff is purely
  additive on top of engine #30 (one counter, one snapshot, one guarded increment, one METRICS field + comments):
  no gate, cap, schema, control-flow, driver-script, or guardrail (NEVER push/deploy) change; the pinned
  correctness + mechanical-runner conjunction (`verdict.pass && verdict.testsPass && runner.exitCode === 0`) is
  untouched. Gates BOTH passed: `validate-driver.cjs` → PASS and `smoke-driver.cjs` → SMOKE-PASS (5 scenarios,
  23 calls, incl. verify-before-commit + gatekeeper-invocation + FAILING/testsPass-false/runner-red
  BLOCK-with-no-commit paths). md5 `b0e01cb783475f904d1b6ad010710c23`; prior engine (#30) backed up to
  `build-loop.prev.js`.

- **2026-07-05 — PROMOTED (engine #27, SUPERVISOR-authored, user-directed): extend `{fable:true}` to
  `planner` + `decider` in the MODEL table.** Run leverage now concentrates in task selection; EPIC-73
  (the best queue to date) was Fable-designed. Two-line change on engine #26; a plain launch still
  resolves all-Opus/Haiku, so the post-2026-07-08 Fable-free guarantee (#25) is untouched. Gates:
  `pre-run-gate.cjs` → PASS + SMOKE-PASS, md5 `e74da3066f8169f1e7ec951a63c121da`, ledger appended.

- **2026-07-05 — PROMOTED (engine #29, Architect-proposed): RED-METER SHORT-CIRCUIT — stop buying Verifier
  verdicts the commit gate is guaranteed to ignore.** The commit gate is a conjunction
  (`verdict.pass && verdict.testsPass && runner.exitCode === 0`), so once the cheap haiku mechanical
  test-runner reports a non-zero exit, the attempt CANNOT pass no matter what the Opus Verifier says — yet
  the engine still paid a full Opus acceptance review on every mechanically-red build. This change: (1) on
  the build path, when `runner.exitCode !== 0` it sets `verdict = null` and `continue`s to the next attempt
  (skipping the dead Verifier call) — the null-verdict shape every call site already tolerates (same as a
  skip/timeout/throw); (2) the same red-meter skip on the REWORK path (a red rework is already doomed to
  revert); (3) retry feedback now degrades gracefully — a red-meter attempt feeds the retry builder the
  runner's failing tail instead of the old empty prompt; (4) block telemetry falls back to the runner tail
  when there's no verdict. Load-bearing invariants UNCHANGED: nothing commits without a green meter; every
  green-meter build still gets the full Verifier; a MISSING meter (`runner=null`) still gets the Verifier's
  run-it-yourself fallback; the pinned conjunction gate, caps, schemas, METRICS fields, and driver-script
  wiring are all untouched. Gates: `validate-driver.cjs` → PASS + `smoke-driver.cjs` → SMOKE-PASS (5
  scenarios, incl. "mechanical runner-red BLOCKs with NO commit"), md5 `399555a59cd9413dc4d12e4d0abd00c2`.
  Prior workflow backed up to `build-loop.prev.js` (md5 `c7b0abb4a0a218148c5daa19f7991b93`).

- **2026-07-05 — PROMOTED (engine #28, Architect-proposed): BLOCKED-PATH DEBRIS QUARANTINE.** Single-hunk
  change to `blockPrompt` (the only diff vs the promoted workflow). Previously the block agent merely set the
  task to BLOCKED in BACKLOG.md; a failed auto-build (MAX_ATTEMPTS exhausted) left the failed builder's
  UNVERIFIED edits uncommitted in the tree, and the next task's integrator (`git add -A`) swept them into a
  "VERIFIED" commit under another task's label — unreviewed code shipping under borrowed verified provenance
  (this run: T-71.1's 1,636 never-verified lines + `strace.out` rode into 5a84e01/64f6aa3), and post-block
  builders inheriting a red/dirty tree (firstShotVerified collapsed 1/4 vs 4/4, 4/4 on the same builder model).
  Fix: the block agent now (1) writes the BLOCKED note, (2) commits ONLY the planning surfaces
  (BACKLOG/STRATEGY/STRATEGY-ARCHIVE, so uncommitted Planner/Strategist/Decider work survives — a bare reset
  would destroy it, which is why restorePrompt could not be reused verbatim), (3) `git reset --hard HEAD &&
  git clean -fd` to discard only this task's unverified debris (clean respects `.gitignore`), then reports
  `git status`. No push/deploy; no gate, cap, schema, METRICS field, or driver-script wiring changed; same
  single `block:*` agent call. Gatekeeper verified the diff is exactly this one function. BOTH gates passed:
  `validate-driver.cjs` → PASS; `smoke-driver.cjs` → SMOKE-PASS (5 scenarios, incl. runner-red/FAILING-verdict
  BLOCK-with-no-code-commit, all terminated cleanly). Promoted workflow md5 `c7b0abb4a0a218148c5daa19f7991b93`;
  prior workflow preserved as `build-loop.prev.js`.

- **2026-06-26 — PROMOTED: record `panelSize` (the reviewer-panel size) into the run's METRICS stats line so
  cross-run readers can tell a real quality decline from a measurement artifact.** Gatekeeper promoted the
  Architect's candidate; BOTH gates passed (`node scripts/validate-driver.cjs build-loop.next.js` → `PASS`;
  `node scripts/smoke-driver.cjs build-loop.next.js` → `SMOKE-PASS`, 3 scenarios — all-pass commits with
  verify-before-commit [20 agent calls]; FAILING verdict BLOCKs with NO commit; `testsPass:false` BLOCKs with NO
  commit; all terminated cleanly). Prior live engine snapshotted to `build-loop.prev.js` (604 lines); new live
  engine `build-loop.workflow.js` is 619 lines (+15, of which 14 are explanatory comments).
  - **What changed (purely additive telemetry — NO control-flow, gate, cap, schema, or wiring change).** Two
    functional lines only: `const panelSize = reviewers.length`, and injecting `"panelSize":${panelSize}` into the
    existing `stats` METRICS string alongside `avgUsefulness`/`minUsefulness`. The pinned correctness gate
    (`verdict.pass && verdict.testsPass`), the `min()`-based rework trigger, the spend cap, and all driver wiring
    are untouched. Mirrors the prior `endReason`/`reworkReverted`/`humanGated`/`blockedReasons` additive-field
    pattern.
  - **Why it matters (Architect's rationale).** Each task's recorded usefulness is the panel MINIMUM and the run's
    `minUsefulness` is a min-of-mins, so recorded usefulness is monotonically sensitive to panel width: every
    reviewer added can only LOWER a task's min, never raise it. With the Manager having grown the panel to 5, a
    downward drift in `avg/minUsefulness` — the very "quality stall" the Strategist and the `qualityStall`
    preflight flag escalate on — can be partly or wholly an artifact of a widening panel at CONSTANT true quality,
    previously indistinguishable in METRICS. Logging `panelSize` lets readers hold panel size constant when
    interpreting the usefulness trend (did the min fall because work got weaker, or because a lens was added?).
  - **Diff verification.** Confirmed via `diff build-loop.workflow.js build-loop.next.js`: the only non-comment
    changes are the two lines above; the remaining 14 added lines are a comment block. Prior live engine backed up
    to `build-loop.prev.js` before the `mv`.

- **2026-07-05 — PROMOTED (engine #26): commit the VERIFIED build to HEAD *before* attempting rework, so a
  failed rework mechanically restores to that commit instead of committing broken debris under a "VERIFIED"
  label.** Gatekeeper promoted the Architect's candidate; BOTH gates passed
  (`node scripts/validate-driver.cjs build-loop.next.js` → `PASS`; `node scripts/smoke-driver.cjs build-loop.next.js`
  → `SMOKE-PASS`, 5 scenarios — all-pass commits with verify-before-commit [23 agent calls]; FAILING verdict BLOCKs
  with NO commit; `testsPass:false` BLOCKs with NO commit; architect-proposal INVOKES the gatekeeper; mechanical
  runner-red BLOCKs with NO commit; all terminated cleanly). Re-ran both gates against the now-live filename after
  the swap → `PASS` / `SMOKE-PASS`. Prior live engine snapshotted to `build-loop.prev.js` (779 lines); new live
  engine `build-loop.workflow.js` is 810 lines (+31; 7 lines removed, 38 added, of which the large majority is
  explanatory comment).
  - **What changed (ordering of an already-required commit; NO gate, cap, schema, METRICS field, or driver-script
    wiring change).** The Integrate phase now issues the verified build's commit (`preCommit`) BEFORE the rework
    attempt, pinning the passed tree at HEAD. On a rework that BREAKS verification, the fallback no longer runs the
    integrator's `git add -A` over the still-dirty rework debris; instead it invokes a new mechanical
    `restorePrompt(taskId)` that runs `git reset --hard HEAD && git clean -fd` to discard ONLY the uncommitted
    rework debris (git clean respects `.gitignore`, so node_modules etc. are untouched), then reports whether
    `git status --porcelain` is empty. A restore that itself errors is caught and degrades to the old dirty-tree
    behavior (never aborts the run). On a rework that RE-PASSES, the unchanged bottom integrator commits the
    rework's delta on top of the pinned verified commit, so both states live in history. The pinned correctness
    gate (`verdict.pass && verdict.testsPass`), the rework trigger, the single-repair-attempt cap, and the spend
    cap are all untouched — only WHEN the already-required commit happens moves earlier.
  - **Why it matters (Architect's rationale).** The pre-#26 snapshot preserved the verified build's METADATA but
    not its FILE EDITS: those were still uncommitted when a rework builder edited the same tree, so on a failed
    rework the integrator's `git add -A` committed the BROKEN rework edits (code that had just FAILED the runner
    or Verifier) under a "VERIFIED" label with the pre-rework summary — the "kept verified pre-rework build" was a
    fiction at the file level, and a runner-red rework could land a RED suite in history (guardrail 6) for the next
    task to inherit. METRICS-backed and newly urgent: since the usefulness-floor widened to `<=3` (+ harsh-dissent
    trigger), rework fires 3-5x/run and the last four runs show `reworkReverted` 2,1,0,2 — five fake reverts in
    four runs. Pinning the verified tree in git first makes the fallback real.
  - **Diff verification.** Confirmed via `diff build-loop.workflow.js build-loop.next.js` before the swap: change
    is localized to the Integrate/rework block plus the new `restorePrompt` template; no control-flow outside that
    block, no gate/cap/schema/wiring edits. Prior live engine backed up to `build-loop.prev.js` before the `mv`;
    candidate `build-loop.next.js` consumed by the `mv` (no longer present).

- **2026-07-02 — PROMOTED: DISSENTER-ONLY post-rework re-score (engine #24) — after a successful rework, only the
  reviewers who actually triggered it re-vote; the satisfied reviewers' original votes stand.** Gatekeeper promoted
  the Architect's candidate; BOTH gates passed (`node scripts/validate-driver.cjs build-loop.next.js` → `PASS`;
  `node scripts/smoke-driver.cjs build-loop.next.js` → `SMOKE-PASS`, 3 scenarios — all-pass commits with
  verify-before-commit [20 agent calls]; FAILING verdict BLOCKs with NO commit; `testsPass:false` BLOCKs with NO
  commit; all terminated cleanly). Re-ran both gates against the now-live `build-loop.workflow.js` post-`mv` →
  still `PASS` / `SMOKE-PASS`. Prior live engine snapshotted to `build-loop.prev.js` (652 lines); new live engine
  `build-loop.workflow.js` is 683 lines (+31, of which the large majority are explanatory comments).
  - **What changed (efficiency; narrows WHO re-votes, no gate/cap/schema/METRICS/wiring change).** (1) The panel
    `median` aggregator is HOISTED from inside `runPanel` to module scope (line 326) so both scoring paths collapse
    votes with the identical function — no new/duplicate declaration (`node --check` clean; `grep 'const median'`
    → exactly one). (2) `runPanel(b, suffix, subset)` gained an optional `subset` param (defaults to the FULL panel
    — unchanged behavior) and now also RETURNS the per-reviewer `votes` array (`{reviewer, ...v}`). (3) The
    post-rework re-score computes `dissenters` = reviewers whose ORIGINAL vote set `needsRework` or scored `<=3`;
    when `0 < dissenters < panel`, only those reviewers re-vote on the amended code and the result is merged with
    the satisfied reviewers' original votes, then re-aggregated through the same module-scope `median`.
  - **Why it matters (Architect's rationale).** The prior engine re-ran the FULL panel on every successful rework
    (panelSize Opus reviews each), even though rework exists to answer the dissenters — the satisfied 4/5 votes are
    not what triggered it. At panelSize=5 with rework firing 3–5×/run, that was ~10–20 Opus calls/run re-collecting
    votes that already existed. Re-voting only the dissenters removes that redundant Opus spend while keeping the
    recorded post-rework usefulness faithful to what shipped.
  - **Correctness review (Gatekeeper).** Verified the conservative edges hold in code, not just comment: a
    dissenter whose re-vote ERRORS is dropped by `runPanel`'s `.filter(Boolean)`, so `re.votes.find(...) || v`
    keeps that reviewer's ORIGINAL (low) vote — a dropped vote can never inflate the score. If no per-reviewer
    votes exist (panel itself errored → fallback `{reworkNotes:[],usefulness:3}` with no `votes`; guarded by
    `panel.votes || []`) or ALL reviewers dissented (`dissenters.length < reviewers.length` false), it falls back
    to the full re-panel exactly as before. The pinned correctness gate (`verdict.pass && verdict.testsPass`) and
    the graceful revert-to-verified-build path are upstream and untouched.
  - **Diff verification.** Confirmed via `diff build-loop.workflow.js build-loop.next.js` (8 removed / 39 added
    lines): the removed lines are the in-`runPanel` local `median` and the two-field return; functional additions
    are the module-scope `median`, the `subset`/`votes` threading, and the dissenter-branch. Prior live engine
    backed up to `build-loop.prev.js` before the `mv`.

- **2026-07-01 — PROMOTED: aggregate each task's per-reviewer usefulness votes by the MEDIAN instead of the
  MINIMUM (`u.length ? median(u) : 3`), so recorded usefulness is robust to a lone outlier vote and stable as the
  panel widens.** Gatekeeper promoted the Architect's candidate; BOTH gates passed (`node
  scripts/validate-driver.cjs build-loop.next.js` → `PASS`; `node scripts/smoke-driver.cjs build-loop.next.js` →
  `SMOKE-PASS`, 3 scenarios — all-pass commits with verify-before-commit [20 agent calls]; FAILING verdict BLOCKs
  with NO commit; `testsPass:false` BLOCKs with NO commit; all terminated cleanly). Prior live engine snapshotted
  to `build-loop.prev.js` (619 lines); new live engine `build-loop.workflow.js` is 637 lines (+18, of which all
  but the two functional lines are an explanatory comment block).
  - **What changed (one hunk at ~line 435 — NO gate, cap, schema, or wiring change).** Two functional lines: a
    `median` helper `const median = (xs) => { const s = [...xs].sort((a, b) => a - b); return s[Math.ceil(s.length
    / 2) - 1] }`, and the return `usefulness: u.length ? median(u) : 3` replacing the previous `Math.min(...u)`.
    The pinned correctness gate (`verdict.pass && verdict.testsPass`) is upstream and untouched; the
    `usefulness<=3` rework trigger, the METRICS `avg`/`minUsefulness` fields, and both driver scripts are
    unchanged — only HOW the same per-task votes collapse to one number. Empty-panel default (3) unchanged;
    even-panel median takes the LOWER of the two central votes (conservative — still leans toward flagging weak
    work).
  - **Why it matters (Architect's rationale).** The prior `panelSize` upgrade (2026-06-26 above) DIAGNOSED but did
    not FIX a structural bias: recorded usefulness was the panel MIN and the run's `minUsefulness` a min-of-mins,
    so the score fell monotonically as the Manager grew the panel (now 5 reviewers) — every lens added can only
    LOWER a task's min. With min-of-5 a single harsh reviewer floors the whole task's score (four 5s and one 2
    record a "2"), the flat "min stuck at 3, avg ~3.75, worst min 2" plateau the `qualityStall` flag, Strategist,
    and Manager kept escalating on for ~25 runs — now known (via the `panelSize` confound) to be partly a
    widening-panel artifact at constant true quality. The median is the minimal robust fix: one reviewer can no
    longer veto the score, it is panel-width-stable (adding a lens no longer mechanically drops the number), yet
    it still surfaces GENUINE low-leverage work (if the MAJORITY scores low the median is low), so the rework
    trigger and cross-run stall detectors keep firing on real plateaus while no longer firing on a lone dissenter.
    This addresses the pending "min()→median" engine-efficiency finding.
  - **Diff verification.** Confirmed via `diff build-loop.workflow.js build-loop.next.js` before the `mv`: exactly
    one changed region (`435c435,453`), 20 diff lines, the only non-comment changes being the two lines above; the
    remaining added lines are a single comment block. Prior live engine backed up to `build-loop.prev.js` before
    the `mv`.

- **2026-06-26 — PROMOTED: raise the in-band rework trigger from panel-min usefulness `<=2` to `<=3`, so the
  modal correct-but-mediocre `3/5` deliverable gets one in-band polish attempt before shipping instead of
  trailing the cross-run plateau detector by a run.** Gatekeeper promoted the Architect's candidate; BOTH gates
  passed (`node scripts/validate-driver.cjs build-loop.next.js` → `PASS`; `node scripts/smoke-driver.cjs
  build-loop.next.js` → `SMOKE-PASS`, 3 scenarios — all-pass commits with verify-before-commit [20 agent calls];
  FAILING verdict BLOCKs with NO commit; `testsPass:false` BLOCKs with NO commit; all terminated cleanly). Prior
  live engine snapshotted to `build-loop.prev.js` (45911 B); new live engine `build-loop.workflow.js` is 46825 B
  (~2.0% larger).
  - **What changed (single focused hunk — NO gate, cap, schema, or wiring change; +17/−13 lines, confined to the
    Critique stage; total diff 34 lines).** The in-band rework guard threshold moved from
    `!reworkNotes.length && usefulness <= 2` to `!reworkNotes.length && usefulness <= 3`, with the synthesized
    rework note reworded to name the long-run quality plateau and to instruct "change as little as possible" if a
    deliverable genuinely caps at 3. Everything else is identical: it still fires the existing rework path only
    when there is NO explicit reviewer note, threads into the unchanged `if (reworkNotes.length)` block,
    snapshots the already-verified pre-rework build, makes exactly ONE repair attempt, re-runs the pinned
    correctness gate, falls back to the verified pre-rework build on rework failure (no unverified commit), and
    re-scores on success.
  - **Why it's safe / both gates' verdicts.** Strictly a threshold widening on an already-promoted additive
    branch: the guard still requires `!reworkNotes.length`, so it cannot suppress or override an explicit rework
    request — it only widens WHEN the one-shot polish pass runs. The Architect's rationale (captured in the diff
    comments): over ~25 runs `minUsefulness` sat at exactly 3 on 11 of them (the dominant value) with
    `avgUsefulness` clustered at 3.75 — a flat-mediocre plateau the `<=2` floor fired on only twice; the
    `qualityStall` MIN-FLOOR PLATEAU clause already recognises this pattern but only escalates it a run later,
    after the 3/5 work has shipped. It cannot thrash or loop (exactly one repair attempt per task, no inner
    loop), and a rework that fails to lift the score still commits the already-verified build, so a task that
    genuinely caps at 3 costs one extra attempt, once. `reworkReverted` was 0 in 17/18 recorded runs, so the
    fallback path is near-never exercised. The static validator confirmed all invariants hold (`PASS`); the
    semantic smoke harness confirmed verify-before-commit, both BLOCK-with-no-commit failure paths, and clean
    termination (`SMOKE-PASS`).

- **2026-06-26 — PROMOTED: a panel-min usefulness of `<=2` now triggers the EXISTING rework machinery even
  when no reviewer set an explicit `needsRework` note — so a correct-but-hard-low-leverage deliverable gets one
  in-band polish attempt before shipping, instead of sailing through uncritiqued and only surfacing a run later
  as a quality-stall trend regression.** Gatekeeper promoted the Architect's candidate; BOTH gates passed
  (`node scripts/validate-driver.cjs build-loop.next.js` → `PASS`; `node scripts/smoke-driver.cjs
  build-loop.next.js` → `SMOKE-PASS`, 3 scenarios — all-pass commits with verify-before-commit [20 agent calls];
  FAILING verdict BLOCKs with NO commit; `testsPass:false` BLOCKs with NO commit; all terminated cleanly). Prior
  live engine snapshotted to `build-loop.prev.js` (44108 B); new live engine `build-loop.workflow.js` is 45911 B
  (~4.1% larger).
  - **What changed (focused, additive rework-trigger diff — NO gate, cap, schema, or wiring change; +17/−1
    lines, confined to the Critique stage).** `reworkNotes` became a `let`, and a new guard fires the existing
    rework path when `!reworkNotes.length && usefulness <= 2`: it synthesizes a single actionable rework note
    from the panel's own hard-low score (instructing the builder to raise real leverage WITHOUT weakening or
    deleting any test) and logs a `usefulness-floor` line. It threads straight into the unchanged
    `if (reworkNotes.length)` block, which snapshots the already-verified pre-rework build, attempts the rework,
    re-runs the pinned correctness gate (`reworkVerdict.pass && reworkVerdict.testsPass`), falls back to the
    verified pre-rework build (no commit of unverified code) if rework breaks verification, and re-scores the
    amended code on success. The `<=2` threshold mirrors the same MIN-OUTLIER threshold the qualityStall
    detector already keys off. Rationale captured in the diff comments: METRICS shows `minUsefulness:2` shipped
    on 2026-06-25 and 2026-06-26 with the rework count spent on OTHER tasks, so a 2/5 deliverable shipped
    uncritiqued and only surfaced later as a quality-stall signal downstream roles react to AFTER it has already
    polluted the avg/min trend; this catches it in-band.
  - **Why it's safe / both gates' verdicts.** The new branch is strictly additive — it only fires when there is
    NO existing reviewer note (`!reworkNotes.length`), so it can never suppress or override an explicit rework
    request; it only WIDENS when the polish pass runs. It reuses the rework path verbatim, so the correctness
    re-gate, the graceful fallback to the verified pre-rework build, and the post-rework re-score are all
    unchanged. The static validator returned `PASS`, confirming all protected invariants remain present in
    executable code (correctness gate `verdict.pass && verdict.testsPass` used as a conditional guard, the

    returned `SMOKE-PASS`, confirming verify-before-commit on the happy path and BLOCK-with-no-commit on both

    only the `let reworkNotes` retype and the new usefulness-floor block differ. Promoted.

- **2026-06-25 — PROMOTED: The mechanical `qualityStall` trigger gains a fourth clause, MIN-FLOOR PLATEAU,
  so a sustained FLAT-MEDIOCRE plateau (`avgUsefulness` hovering ~3.75, `minUsefulness` stuck at 3 and never
  climbing to 4) now fires the trigger — closing the gap where work that neither DECLINES nor produces a hard
  `<=2` outlier still never reaches high leverage and previously slipped through.** Gatekeeper promoted the
  Architect's candidate; BOTH gates passed (`node scripts/validate-driver.cjs build-loop.next.js` → `PASS`;
  `node scripts/smoke-driver.cjs build-loop.next.js` → `SMOKE-PASS`, 3 scenarios — all-pass commits with

  engine `build-loop.workflow.js` is 42798 B.
  - **What changed (focused diff — prompt text only; NO control-flow, schema, loop, gate, cap, or guardrail
    change).** Building on the prior MIN-OUTLIER upgrade, this adds a fourth named clause, (d) MIN-FLOOR PLATEAU,
    to the rule the Preflight agent applies to derive the same `qualityStall` boolean from the same last-5
    METRICS window. The trigger is now an OR of four clauses: (a) AVG-DECLINE, (b) AVG-FLOOR, (c) MIN-OUTLIER
    (all pre-existing), and (d) the new MIN-FLOOR PLATEAU — fires when `minUsefulness` has been `<=3` on the 2+
    most recent consecutive runs (every recent batch shipped at least one barely-useful sub-4 deliverable, two
    or more runs running). Clause (d) exists because (a)/(b)/(c) all key off either a DECLINE or a hard `<=2`
    OUTLIER, so a sustained flat-mediocre plateau (avg ~3.75, min stuck at 3, never climbing to 4) trips none of
    them and slips through — yet a min that never reaches 4 across consecutive runs IS the correct-but-low-
    leverage stall the loop must escalate. It mirrors (b)'s AVG-FLOOR shape (2+ consecutive recent runs), so a
    single good run (min>=4) immediately clears it and it will not thrash on run-to-run noise. The diff is
    exactly +7 lines of prompt text in the `preflightPrompt` `qualityStall` derivation block; nothing else
    differs from `build-loop.prev.js`.

- **2026-06-25 — PROMOTED: The mechanical `qualityStall` trigger now also catches a single low-leverage

- **2026-06-24 — PROMOTED: make `endReason` HONEST — stop labeling a truncated/stalled run as a completed
  batch.** Gatekeeper promoted the Architect's candidate; BOTH gates passed
  (`node scripts/validate-driver.cjs build-loop.next.js` → `PASS`;
  `node scripts/smoke-driver.cjs build-loop.next.js` → `SMOKE-PASS`, 3 scenarios — all-pass commits with

  - **What changed (single, focused diff — two hunks, telemetry only).** The `endReason` field's whole purpose

    fall-through where `iter` never reached `MAX_ITERS` and no break fired — exactly masquerading a frontier
    drain/stall as a completed batch. With `verified` pinned at 4 for 11 runs while `MAX_ITERS=8`, METRICS had
    been logging `endReason:"iters"` on runs that built only 4. The candidate adds, right after the existing
    `rounds`-cap relabel, one post-loop line: `if (iter < MAX_ITERS && endReason === 'iters') endReason =
    'drained'`. `'iters'` now means `iter===MAX_ITERS` ONLY; any other fall-through with `iter<MAX_ITERS` (the
    Planner stopped yielding ready work without the strategist-dry break firing) is labeled `'drained'`. The
    accompanying `endReason` documentation comment was updated to describe the new `drained` value.
