    protected invariants intact (correctness gate, HARD GUARDRAILS block, MAX_ITERS/MAX_ROUNDS caps, both
    self-upgrade gate wirings). Smoke harness ran the engine end-to-end (20 agent calls, clean termination,
    verify-before-commit confirmed). Candidate grew (31585 B → 32319 B), well clear of the anti-gutting floor.

- **2026-06-23 — PROMOTED: act on the `humanGated` signal — when it is standing/growing, sharpen the
  blocking needs-human proposal and prefer work that unblocks it, instead of inventing more incremental
  tasks around the dam.** Gatekeeper promoted the Architect's candidate; BOTH gates passed
  (`node scripts/validate-driver.cjs build-loop.next.js` → `PASS`;
  `node scripts/smoke-driver.cjs build-loop.next.js` → `SMOKE-PASS`, 20 agent calls, terminated cleanly,
  verify-before-commit confirmed). Prior live engine snapshotted to `build-loop.prev.js` (30814 B); new
  engine is 31585 B.
  - **What changed (single, focused diff in the Planner prompt).** A prior upgrade made `humanGated`
    mechanically visible by logging it to METRICS; this upgrade closes the loop by telling the Planner what
    to *do* about it. The Planner step now also inspects the `humanGated` field across recent runs: a
    non-zero count that persists/grows across multiple runs is flagged as a VALUE CEILING — the
    highest-leverage work is dammed behind an unresolved human decision (real funds/deploy/securities/legal)
    and the loop is being forced into lower-leverage work around it. On detecting a persistent `humanGated`
    count the Planner is instructed NOT to merely invent more incremental tasks, but to identify the
    blocking needs-human proposal in STRATEGY.md and SHARPEN it into a crisp, decision-ready ask, and to
    prefer auto-buildable work that de-risks or directly unblocks that proposal once the human acts. The
    diff is a single contiguous insertion into the existing planning instruction (9 changed lines).
  - **Why low-risk / invariants preserved.** Change is prompt-only, confined to the Planner instruction
    text; no control flow, gate, or guardrail logic touched. Validator confirmed all protected invariants
    intact: correctness gate (`verdict.pass && verdict.testsPass`), HARD GUARDRAILS block,
    MAX_ITERS/MAX_ROUNDS caps, and both self-upgrade gate wirings (`scripts/validate-driver.cjs` +
    `scripts/smoke-driver.cjs`). Candidate grew (30814 B → 31585 B), well clear of the anti-gutting floor.

- **2026-06-23 — PROMOTED: a failed USEFULNESS rework no longer destroys already-verified work —
  fall back to the verified pre-rework build and commit it instead of BLOCKING the task.** Gatekeeper
  promoted the Architect's candidate; BOTH gates passed (`node scripts/validate-driver.cjs
  build-loop.next.js` → `PASS`; `node scripts/smoke-driver.cjs build-loop.next.js` → `SMOKE-PASS`,
  20 agent calls, terminated cleanly, verify-before-commit confirmed). Prior live engine snapshotted to
  `build-loop.prev.js` (29668 B); new engine is 30814 B.
  - **What changed (single, focused diff in the Critique/rework step).** Previously, when a task passed
    the pinned correctness gate but a reviewer requested a usefulness-polish rework, a rework that then
    *broke* verification caused the whole task to be marked `BLOCKED` — throwing away the already-verified,
    shippable pre-rework build over a failed cosmetic polish. The candidate snapshots the verified
    `build`/`verdict` before rework (`verifiedBuild`/`verifiedVerdict`), runs the rework into separate
    `reworkBuild`/`reworkVerdict` vars, and: if the rework re-passes the gate, adopts the amended code and
    re-scores it; if the rework fails or errors, falls back to the verified pre-rework build, commits it as
    `VERIFIED` (flagged `reworkReverted:true`, usefulness = the pre-rework panel score that actually ships)
    instead of blocking. Net effect: verified value is never discarded by a failed quality-polish attempt.
  - **Why low-risk / invariants preserved.** The pinned correctness gate is intact: the rework path still
    requires `reworkVerdict.pass && reworkVerdict.testsPass` before adopting amended code, and the main
    build/verify gate (`verdict.pass && verdict.testsPass`) is untouched — nothing is ever committed that
    did not pass verification. HARD GUARDRAILS block, MAX_ITERS/MAX_ROUNDS caps, and the wiring of both
    `scripts/validate-driver.cjs` and `scripts/smoke-driver.cjs` are all unchanged (verified by diff).

- **2026-06-23 — PROMOTED: log the human-gated backlog size (`humanGated`) to METRICS, so a value
  CEILING is mechanically visible across runs.** Gatekeeper promoted the Architect's candidate; BOTH gates
  passed (`node scripts/validate-driver.cjs build-loop.next.js` → `PASS`;
  `node scripts/smoke-driver.cjs build-loop.next.js` → `SMOKE-PASS`, 20 agent calls, terminated cleanly,
  verify-before-commit confirmed). Prior live engine snapshotted to `build-loop.prev.js` (27686 B); new
  engine is 28747 B.
  - **What changed (single, focused diff in the Report/telemetry step).** Added a `nHumanGated` field —
    `((lastPlan && lastPlan.humanGated) || []).length` — to the `stats` line appended to
    `docs/METRICS.jsonl` (plus an explanatory comment). The Planner already separates `humanGated` tasks
    (real funds/deploy/securities/legal — never auto-buildable) from buildable work, but that count was
    only ever returned in the result object and surfaced in prose, never logged to METRICS. A
    standing/growing `humanGated` count is the signal the Strategist (quality stagnation) and Manager
    already read: when usefulness declines while the loop keeps verifying, it tells them the
    highest-leverage work is dammed up behind an unresolved human decision and to sharpen the needs-human
    proposal rather than treat the dip as an unexplained quality regression.
  - **Why low-risk / invariants preserved.** Change is confined to the Report/telemetry block; `lastPlan`
    is already defined and null-guarded, control flow is unchanged. Validator confirmed all protected
    invariants intact: correctness gate (`verdict.pass && verdict.testsPass`), HARD GUARDRAILS block,
    MAX_ITERS/MAX_ROUNDS caps, and both self-upgrade gate wirings (`scripts/validate-driver.cjs` +
    `scripts/smoke-driver.cjs`). Candidate size (28747 B) is well above the 60% anti-gutting floor of the
    prior engine (27686 B).

- **2026-06-23 — PROMOTED: re-score usefulness after a successful rework (record what actually
  shipped, not the stale pre-rework score).** Gatekeeper promoted the Architect's candidate; BOTH gates
  passed (`node scripts/validate-driver.cjs build-loop.next.js` → `PASS`;
  `node scripts/smoke-driver.cjs build-loop.next.js` → `SMOKE-PASS`, 20 agent calls, terminated cleanly,
  verify-before-commit confirmed). Prior live engine snapshotted to `build-loop.prev.js` (26660 B); new
  engine is 27686 B.
  - **What changed (single, focused diff at the Critique/rework step).** The dynamic review panel was
    extracted into a reusable `runPanel(b, suffix)` helper (identical logic for both the initial critique
    and the post-rework re-critique, so the two paths cannot diverge). When the panel requests rework and
    the Builder's amended work re-passes verification, the engine now re-runs the same panel against the
    AMENDED code and records THAT usefulness, instead of committing the stale pre-rework score. Previously
    a successful rework — the loop's own mechanism for raising quality — was logged in METRICS as if quality
    never improved, polluting the `avgUsefulness`/`minUsefulness` trend the Strategist reads for quality
    stagnation and the Manager reads to reshape the team.
  - **Why low-risk / invariants preserved.** Change is confined to the Critique/rework block; control flow
    is unchanged (rework that breaks verification still BLOCKs via the existing path, never commits).
    Validator confirmed all protected invariants intact: correctness gate (`verdict.pass &&
    verdict.testsPass`), HARD GUARDRAILS block, MAX_ITERS/MAX_ROUNDS caps, and both self-upgrade gate
    wirings (`scripts/validate-driver.cjs` + `scripts/smoke-driver.cjs`). Candidate size (27686 B) is well
    above the 60% anti-gutting floor of the prior engine (26660 B).

- **2026-06-23 — PROMOTED (operator-applied during failure recovery): make a single agent error
  non-fatal to the run.** Applied by the supervising operator, NOT the Architect agent, because this
  failure mode prevents the loop from ever reaching its own Architect phase (so it cannot self-heal it).
  Promoted via the identical Gatekeeper path and gates: BOTH passed (`validate-driver.cjs` → `PASS`;
  `smoke-driver.cjs` → `SMOKE-PASS`, verify-before-commit confirmed). Prior engine snapshotted to
  `build-loop.prev.js`.
  - **Signal.** 2 of 5 runs (run #1 `wf_6517d765`, run #5 `wf_c69f4020`) died on
    `StructuredOutput retry cap (5) exceeded` — in both cases a Builder that had finished its work (suite
    left green) but could not emit its summary object. The unhandled throw propagated out of the main
    loop and aborted the ENTIRE workflow, discarding the Manager/Report/Architect end-phases and forcing
    manual recovery of the in-flight task. Because the run dies before the Architect runs, the loop can
    never propose a fix for this itself.
  - **What changed (two `try/catch` wraps only).** The per-task build+verify attempt loop and the rework
    build+verify are wrapped so a thrown agent error is treated as a failed attempt (`verdict = null`):
    it retries up to `MAX_ATTEMPTS`, then the task is BLOCKED via the existing path and the loop CONTINUES
    to the next task and its end-phases. No other logic touched.
  - **Why safe / invariants preserved.** The correctness gate is unchanged — a task still only commits
    when `verdict.pass && verdict.testsPass`; a thrown/`null` verdict can only BLOCK, never commit (smoke
    test re-confirmed verify-before-commit). HARD GUARDRAILS, MAX_ITERS/MAX_ROUNDS, and both gate wirings
    intact (validator PASS). This RESTORES the loop's ability to reach its Architect, which can harden the
    remaining phases (plan/strategize/manager) further on its own behind the gates.

- **2026-06-23 — PROMOTED: persist usefulness telemetry to METRICS.jsonl.** Gatekeeper promoted the
  Architect's candidate; BOTH gates passed (`node scripts/validate-driver.cjs` → `PASS`;
  `node scripts/smoke-driver.cjs` → `SMOKE-PASS`, 20 agent calls, terminated cleanly, verify-before-commit
  confirmed). Prior live engine snapshotted to `build-loop.prev.js`.
  - **What changed (single, focused diff at the Report step).** The per-task `usefulness` signal computed
    during Critique was previously consumed only by the Manager's ephemeral run-summary and then dropped.
    The candidate now derives `avgUsefulness` (mean, 2-dp rounded) and `minUsefulness` across this run's
    VERIFIED tasks and appends both to the `stats` string written as one JSON line to
    `docs/METRICS.jsonl`. Both are `null` when no task verified. This makes quality stagnation (e.g. a
    multi-run plateau at 4/5 — the exact pattern the Manager has been flagging by hand) mechanically
    visible across runs instead of reconstructable only from prose.
  - **Why low-risk / invariants preserved.** Change is confined to telemetry assembly; no control flow,
    no agent wiring touched. Validator confirmed all protected invariants intact: correctness gate
    (`verdict.pass && verdict.testsPass`), HARD GUARDRAILS block, MAX_ITERS/MAX_ROUNDS caps, and both
    self-upgrade gate wirings (`scripts/validate-driver.cjs` + `scripts/smoke-driver.cjs`). Candidate
    size (25323 B) is well above the 60% anti-gutting floor of the prior engine (24652 B).

- **2026-06-23 — PROMOTED: teach the Strategist to read the usefulness trend and act on quality
  stagnation.** Gatekeeper promoted the Architect's candidate; BOTH gates passed
  (`node scripts/validate-driver.cjs build-loop.next.js` → `PASS`;
  `node scripts/smoke-driver.cjs build-loop.next.js` → `SMOKE-PASS`, 20 agent calls, terminated
  cleanly, verify-before-commit confirmed). Prior live engine snapshotted to `build-loop.prev.js`
  (25323 B); new engine is 25906 B.
  - **What changed (single, focused diff in `strategistPrompt`).** This is the natural follow-on to the
    previous upgrade, which began persisting `avgUsefulness`/`minUsefulness` to `docs/METRICS.jsonl` but
    left nothing reading them. The candidate now instructs the Strategist to FIRST read the last ~5 lines
    of `docs/METRICS.jsonl` and inspect the `avgUsefulness`/`minUsefulness` trend: if tasks keep verifying
    but usefulness has plateaued or is flat-and-mediocre (e.g. avg stuck at the same value with no upward
    movement), treat that as QUALITY STAGNATION and change approach materially — pursue higher-leverage
    work (a capability that unlocks new value, a pivot, or removing what isn't paying off) rather than
    more incremental items in the same vein. The pre-existing `stagnation >= 2` warning (zero verified
    progress) is unchanged; this adds a second, orthogonal stagnation signal (correct-but-low-leverage
    output) that the prior telemetry upgrade made mechanically observable.
  - **Why low-risk / invariants preserved.** Change is confined to one prompt string; no control flow,
    no caps, no agent wiring touched. Validator confirmed all protected invariants intact: correctness
    gate (`verdict.pass && verdict.testsPass`), HARD GUARDRAILS block, MAX_ITERS/MAX_ROUNDS caps, and
    both self-upgrade gate wirings (`scripts/validate-driver.cjs` + `scripts/smoke-driver.cjs`). The
    smoke harness ran the engine end-to-end with stubbed agents and it terminated cleanly with the
    verify-before-commit ordering confirmed. Candidate size is above the 60% anti-gutting floor.

  - **Why this is a TEAM defect (a coverage gap), not just a product pivot.** I audited which lens owns EPIC-51's
    load-bearing correctness-and-honesty invariants — and none squarely does. TrustIntegrity's existing sections own
    seal/license/money inside `cli/`+`trustledger/` (its `revoke`-ish text was only the license-EXPIRY entitlement clock,
    an unrelated surface); VerifierIndependence owns the standalone `verifier/` tree (revocation lives in `cli/core/` +
    the four CLI verify paths, not that tree); Critic owns market-fit; Operability owns output/HTTP shape; Security owns
    classic vuln classes. So the make-or-break revocation invariants had NO dedicated owner: (a) the SELF-CONTROL
    invariant (a key revokes ITSELF — recovered signer must equal the embedded `vendorAddress`, or a third party could
    grief any vendor by "revoking" their key); (b) IGNORE-INVALID-NEVER-DOWNGRADE (a forged revocation must be ignored,
    never trusted to flip a verdict); (c) the NON-LOOSENING invariant (no `--revocations` => byte-identical verdict/exit
    to before EPIC-51; a revocation can ONLY turn ACCEPTED into REVOKED, never the reverse); (d) the AS-OF WINDOW
    soundness (a later-dated revocation KEEPS ACCEPTED with an informational note — the forensic "signed while the key
    was good" value — with sound strict-ISO comparison and no boundary off-by-one); (e) the HONEST BOUNDARY (a revocation
    is a SIGNED CLAIM, NOT a trusted wall-clock timestamp without P-3). A subtle bug in any of these is a silent
    over-trust hole OR a downgrade-griefing vector that a naive unit test passes — the exact "passing test still misses a
    trust defect" class TrustIntegrity exists for. EPIC-51 is the Strategist's declared lead surface for the coming runs,
    so the gap will recur every run until a lens owns it.
  - **The change (extend the closest correctness lens; reuse its proven scrutiny pattern).** I added a KEY-LIFECYCLE /
    REVOCATION + TRUST-DECISION-AS-OF section to TrustIntegrity (placed before the fulfillment/license/seal sections) that
    holds each invariant above as a hard line, demands the verifier RE-DERIVE the signer from embedded bytes (never trust
    the file's claims), requires the non-loosening invariant be pinned by a regression test, and forbids any forked
    signing/recovery path (must reuse `cli/core/attestation.js` VERBATIM — no new crypto/dependency). Vendor-key hygiene
    and REVENUE INTEGRITY (a revocation is a signed claim, not a token/tradeable/appreciating asset) carry over verbatim.
    This mirrors exactly how TrustIntegrity already grew to own the seal and the fulfillment adapter as those surfaces
    shipped — same lens, one more make-or-break class, no roster churn.
  - **Why NOT a sixth reviewer / why NOT re-aim Critic.** A 6th lens for a single cross-cutting primitive is thrash and
    over-budget; the primitive's failure modes are correctness-and-honesty, which is precisely TrustIntegrity's charter,
    so extending it is the lower-thrash, higher-coherence move. Critic is already correctly aimed at the EVIDENCE
    funnel/leverage axis (re-aimed 2026-06-25) and EPIC-51 de-risks that same P-7 path, so no Critic change is warranted.
    No builder-profile change: the `cli` and `trustledger` personas already cover the pure-core + signed-attestation-reuse
    + filesystem-isolation discipline EPIC-51 needs.

    on BOTH the server `renderHTML` path and the browser `escapeHtml` path; (e) UI/DISCLAIMER DRIFT — the page
    is shipped as `public/index.html` AND duplicated as a byte-faithful `embeddedIndexHtml()` fallback, two
    copies of the UI + the custodian/tamper-evidence disclaimer that can silently diverge; (f) DEPLOY POSTURE
    (loopback bind, no auth/no CORS by default — correct for a local broker door, but must not drift toward an
    unauthenticated public bind, and hosting/auth/TLS stay needs-human). Operability's lens was explicitly

    Critic owns market-fit. None owned the HTTP/web surface — which is exactly where the next batch of work

- **2026-06-24 — Manager: MODIFY TrustIntegrity (+ sharpen the `trustledger` builder profile) to OWN the
  seal / tamper-evidence surface — the one thing this run actually churned on. Roster stays 3 reviewers
  (Critic + Operability + TrustIntegrity) and 4 builder profiles (no add/remove, no thrash); the change is a
  targeted re-aim of the make-or-break lens onto the NEW make-or-break surface.**
  - **The signal (this run, not recited).** 100% TrustLedger again, but NOT a clean validation like the prior
    two runs: T-25.3 VERIFIED 3/5; T-25.4 VERIFIED 4/5 [2x]; **T-26.1 VERIFIED 4/5 [3x rework]**; T-26.2
    VERIFIED 3/5. The rework concentrated HARD on EPIC-26 — the reconciliation SEAL (`trustledger/seal.js` +
    `vh trust reconcile --seal` + `vh trust verify-seal`), which deliberately bridges TrustLedger into the
    project's provenance core (`cli/core/manifest.js`, `cli/hash.js` hashEntries/pathLeaf/buildTree, the shared
    attestation envelope). T-26.1 (the pure seal core) took THREE rework cycles and T-26.2 landed at 3/5. Three
    consecutive "HOLD" runs had clean single-rework, 4-verified loops; this one did not. That churn is a real
    coverage signal, not normal variance.
  - **The gap the old roster left uncovered (confirmed in code).** I read `trustledger/seal.js` end-to-end. The
    seal's entire value is a cryptographic-binding property: a content-addressed Merkle `root` over {source
    inputs + every emitted packet file + a synthetic verdict/role HEADER leaf} such that ANY edit/rename/add/
    remove of a file — or any edit of the recorded verdict/reportDate/period, or any swap of an input ROLE —
    changes the root, and `verifySeal` RE-DERIVES from supplied bytes and LOCALIZES the change (MATCH/CHANGED/
    MISSING/UNEXPECTED per file; header for verdict/role). The load-bearing check is "the top-level `root` must
    re-derive from the listed (relPath, contentHash) pairs PLUS the header leaf via the EXACT manifest/contract
    convention." A subtle defect here (a header that is computed but not actually committed to the same root, a
    second/divergent hashing scheme, an order-dependence that should be order-independent, a case/normalization
    mismatch on a root compare, a path-collision/double-count, a verifySeal that could report MATCH for a
    tampered file) DEFEATS the product's entire defensibility value-prop yet passes naive unit tests. That is
    precisely the "a passing test can still miss it" make-or-break class — but it is MONEY-MATH's analogue, not
    money math itself, so the TrustIntegrity lens (scoped to integer-cents + reconciliation arithmetic) did NOT
    own it; Operability's output-shape/filesystem lens explicitly treats the provenance core as "MATURE and
    secondary"; and Critic judges market fit. No lens owned the seal's tamper-evidence correctness — which is
    why the loop churned on it unguided.
  - **The change (minimal, evidence-based).** (1) MODIFY TrustIntegrity: extend its mandate with a SEAL /
    TAMPER-EVIDENCE section that owns the root re-derivation, the verdict/role HEADER-leaf binding, the verbatim
    reuse of the manifest convention (flag any second hashing scheme), order-independence/total-sort,
    case/double-count/path-collision pitfalls, verifySeal's authoritative RE-COMPUTE-and-localize contract,
    purity/determinism/strictness, and the honest tamper-evidence-vs-timestamp-vs-legal-meaning posture
    (SEAL_TRUST_NOTE must never weaken/drift). Same honesty-and-correctness posture it already applies to the
    money math, re-aimed at the surface that actually broke. (2) SHARPEN the `trustledger` builder profile to
    require verbatim core reuse (no re-implemented hashing), the committed verdict/role header, an authoritative
    localizing verifySeal, purity/strictness, and ADVERSARIAL tamper tests (edit a file/verdict/role; drop/add/
    rename a file → assert the root no longer re-derives and verifySeal pinpoints the change). Builder-side,
    because the 3x rework was builder-side on exactly this surface.
  - **Why not other moves.** (a) ADD a 4th reviewer for "seal correctness" — unnecessary thrash; the new
    surface is the SAME correctness-and-honesty class TrustIntegrity already exists for, just on a new artifact,
    so re-aiming the existing lens is cleaner and keeps reviewers at 3. (b) Give it to Operability — it would
    blur Operability's output-shape/hygiene focus and contradict its explicit "provenance core is secondary"
    framing; the seal's risk is cryptographic correctness, not CLI shape. (c) HOLD again — three straight HOLDs
    were correct when loops were clean, but a 3x-rework + 3/5 concentrated on one uncovered surface IS the "real
    signal from this run" the directive asks me to act on. (d) REMOVE `contract` — still saw no Solidity, but
    the seal reuses `cli/hash.js`/the on-chain leaf convention, so the provenance/Solidity line is now LOAD-
    BEARING for TrustLedger again; removing `contract` now would be exactly the wrong moment. EPIC-26 continues
    (T-26.3 docs; the close.js `inputsDigest` gap invites more sealing), so the re-aimed lens will keep paying
    off on the surface ahead, not a one-off.

    that flags a problem nobody is mandated to fix just re-flags it forever. So I folded exactly what

- **2026-06-23 — Manager: MODIFY reviewer "Critic" (add a macro "value-frontier / escalation" lens).**
  Roster unchanged at 2 reviewers (Critic + Operability); no reviewer add/remove; no builder change.
  Single targeted lens edit.
  - **Signal — the 4/5 plateau is no longer a docs artifact; it now caps SUBSTANTIVE work too.** This run
    shipped T-10.3 (docs), B-10.1 (a real capability: thread the lineage `--parent` edge through the
    resumable commit/reveal receipt, schema v4), B-10.2 (docs), and T-11.1 (a real contract task: a frozen
    immutable `REGISTRY_ID` + `REGISTRY_VERSION` + full ERC-165 `supportsInterface`, with a pinned-hash test
    and exhaustive trust-boundary NatSpec). **All four scored 4/5.** That directly contradicts the standing
    Manager/Strategist narrative ("substantive work scores 5/5; only inherently-capped pure-docs tasks hit
    4/5"): I read the T-11.1 contract diff and the B-10.1 thread-through — both are genuinely strong,
    well-tested, well-documented work, and both still landed at 4. Suite 486 green; repo root clean (0
    receipt litter — the Operability/cli-hygiene loop stays closed).
  - **Root cause (confirmed against the repo, not inferred).** The project's real value unlock — EPIC-3
    reputation keyed to verified contributions — is BLOCKED on **D-2 (token framing)**, a human-only
    decision. D-2 is cited as the blocker **15+ times** across STRATEGY.md / BACKLOG.md / docs/MORNING.md,
    and every Strategist run since recites "EPIC-3 is the bigger prize but blocked on D-2 — cannot
    auto-build," then ships incremental scaffolding around an already-complete core (EPIC-6→11). Yet the
    "Proposals — needs-human" section of STRATEGY.md still reads `_(none yet)_`: **D-2 has never been
    written up as a decision-ready proposal a human could actually act on.** So the loop is structurally
    stuck producing correct-but-capped work because the path to >4/5 value is gated behind an escalation
    that nobody is mandated to make. The work is sound; it cannot exceed 4/5 because it is not moving the
    project toward the value the human-gated decision would unlock.
  - **Why a reviewer-lens change (and on Critic, not a new reviewer).** This is a judgment about FINISHED
    work at the macro level ("is this the highest-value reachable step, or are we polishing because the real
    prize is un-escalated?"), so it belongs to a reviewer, not a builder persona. No current lens owns it:
    Critic judged each task's usefulness-vs-busywork in isolation and missed the cross-run pattern;
    Operability owns output/ABI stability + filesystem hygiene (still earning its slot — this run it
    confirmed 0 leaked receipts). Folding the macro "value-frontier / is-the-blocker-escalated" scrutiny
    into Critic is the natural home (it already owns usefulness) and keeps the roster lean at 2 — adding a
    3rd reviewer for one signal would be thrash, and the existing two both demonstrably earn their slots.
  - **Intended effect.** Critic should now flag, when the team is shipping technically-sound but
    value-capped increments, that the right move is to surface the human blocker (D-2 token framing; and
    EPIC-4 deploy) as a sharp, options-and-tradeoffs, recommended-default proposal in the `needs-human`
    section below — turning a 15×-cited dead end into something a human can decide and unblock — rather than
    queueing yet another correct-but-4/5 increment. No builder/profile change, no removal, no thrash.
